Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Grammar and Rhetoric of 'Wa-ba‘du' in Classical Islamic Texts
Commentary on the grammatical and rhetorical function of the transition phrase wa-ba‘du

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the grammatical construction of 'wa-ba‘du' in an Arabic text, determine its case (mabni or mansub) based on the intended meaning, and explain its rhetorical function as a transition marker (fadl al-khitab).

Core Idea
The phrase 'wa-ba‘du' functions as a transition marker; its case depends on whether the omitted noun is intended in meaning or word.

In classical Islamic texts, especially in logical and theological works, the phrase 'wa-ba‘du' signals a shift from the opening praise to the main subject. Understanding its grammatical nuances and rhetorical purpose is essential for interpreting the structure of such works. Al-Bajuri's commentary clarifies this phrase, revealing the depth of Arabic linguistic conventions used in scholarly discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase in its context
Locate 'wa-ba‘du' in the matn. Note that it typically follows the basmalah and praise, serving as a transition to the main subject.
2
Determine the grammatical case
Understand that 'ba‘du' is mabni on damma when the possessive noun is omitted with its meaning intended; it can be mansub if the word of the possessive is intended. The first is more common.
Al-Bajuri explains the two possibilities and notes that the first is more known (الأشهر الأول).
3
Understand temporal vs. locative usage
Recognize that 'ba‘du' is primarily temporal (time) but can also be locative. In the context of a book's introduction, temporal is intended, though locative could be considered for the page position.
The passage gives examples: temporal 'Zayd came after 'Amr' and locative 'Zayd's house after 'Amr's house'.
4
Analyze its rhetorical function
'Wa-ba‘du' is used to transition between discourse types. It is known as 'fadl al-khitab' (the best part of speech). It can be part of the condition or the answer; preferring it as part of the answer makes the subject matter absolute and stronger.
Al-Bajuri prefers the second possibility (part of the answer) and supports it with a more exact reason from a Maghrebi investigator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة الناظم
(۹) وَبَعْدُ: فَالمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِلِلِّسَانِ
الباجوري
بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ حَذَفَ المُضَافَ إِلَيْهِ وَنَوَى مَعْنَاهُ ، وَيَصِحُ فِيهِ النَّصْبُ عَلَى الظَّرْفِيَّةِ ؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ حَذَفَ المُضَافَ إِلَيْهِ وَنَوَى لَفْظَهُ، لَكِنَّ الأَشْهَرَ الأَوَّلُ .
وَيُسْتَعْمَلُ هَذَا الطَّرْفُ لِلزَّمَانِ كَثِيراً ؛ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكَ : جَاءَ زَيْدٌ بَعْدَ عَمْرٍو، وَلِلمَكَانِ قَلِيلاً ؛ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكَ : دَارُ زَيْدٍ بَعْدَ دَارِ عَمْرٍو ، وَالمُتَبَادَرُ هُنَا الأَوَّلُ ، وَإِنْ صَحَ الثَّانِي أَيْضاً بِاعْتِبَارِ مَكَانِ الرَّقْمِ.
وَهَلْ هُوَ مِنْ مَعْمُولَاتِ الشَّرْطِ، أَوْ مِنْ مَعْمُولَاتِ الجَزَاءِ احْتِمَالَانِ، وَالثَّانِي أَوْلَى؛ لِيَكُونَ المُعَلَّقُ عَلَيْهِ مُطْلَقاً ، فَيَكُونَ المُعَلَّقُ أَقْوَى فِي التَّحَقُّقِ ؛ لِأَنَّ المُعَلَّقَ عَلَى المُطْلَقِ أَبْلَغُ فِي التَّحَقُّقِ مِنَ المُعَلَّقِ عَلَى المُقَيِّدِ؛ كَذَا قَالُوا . وَالأَدَقُ فِي تَوْجِيهِ الأُولَوِيَّةِ مَا أَفَادَهُ بَعْضُ مُحَقِّقِي المَغَارِبَةِ مِنْ : أَنَّ ذَلِكَ أَمْثَلُ لِلأَمْرِ بِالبَدَاءَةِ بِالبَسْمَلَةِ وَمَا بَعْدَهَا المَفْهُومُ مِنَ الأَحَادِيثِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ صَرِيحٌ فِي أَنَّ الشُّرُوعَ فِي التَّأْلِيفِ بَعْدَ البَدَاءَةِ بِذَلِكَ، وَلَا كَذَلِكَ الأَوَّلُ.
وَلَا يُؤْتَى بِهَذِهِ العِبَارَةِ إِلَّا عِنْدَ الانْتِقَالِ مِنْ نَوْعٍ مِنَ الكَلَامِ إِلَى نَوْعِ آخَرَ، وَهَذَا هُوَ مَعْنَى مَا اشْتُهِرَ مِنْ : أَنَّ هَذِهِ الكَلِمَةَ هِيَ فَضْلُ الخِطَابِ، كَمَا أَجْمَعَ عَلَيْهِ المُحَقِّقُونَ.
Introduction of the author: (9) And afterwards: The relation of logic to the mind is like the relation of grammar to the tongue. al-Bajuri: Based on the assumption that he omitted the possessive noun and intended its meaning, and it is also correct to put it in the accusative as a time adverb, based on the assumption that he omitted the possessive noun and intended its word, but the first is more known. This adverb is used frequently for time, as in your saying: 'Zayd came after 'Amr', and rarely for place, as in your saying: 'Zayd's house is after 'Amr's house'. The intended here is the first, although the second also applies considering the place of the digit. And whether it is part of the condition (shart) or part of the answer (jaza') are two possibilities. The second is preferable so that the thing on which it is dependent is absolute, making the dependent stronger in actualization, because the dependent on an absolute is more powerful in actualization than the dependent on a restricted one; thus they said. The more exact in directing the preference is what a certain investigator from the Maghreb conveyed: that it is more fitting for the command to begin with the basmalah and what follows it, as understood from the hadiths, because it is explicit that the beginning of the composition is after the start with that. The first is not like that. This phrase is only used when transitioning from one type of discourse to another. This is the meaning of what is well-known: that this word is the 'virtue of speech' (fadl al-khitab), as the verifiers agreed upon.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and rhetorical commentary on the phrase 'wa-ba‘du' (وبعد) that appears in the matn's introductory line. The commentator (al-Bajuri) explains its syntactic construction and usage. First, he addresses why the word 'ba‘du' is in the nominative case with a damma (مبني على الضم). He states that this is because the possessive noun (مضاف إليه) is omitted and its meaning is intended, making it mabni. Alternatively, it could be mansub as a time adverb if the possessive noun's word is intended. The first view is more prevalent. Next, he explains that this adverb is primarily temporal, as in 'Zayd came after 'Amr', but can also be locative, as in 'Zayd's house is after 'Amr's house'. In the context of the matn, the temporal meaning is intended, although a locative meaning could also apply considering the position of the digit (i.e., the page position). Then he discusses whether 'ba‘du' is a modifier of the implied condition (shart) or the answer (jaza'). He prefers the second—that it is part of the answer—because then the thing conditioned (the subject matter) is absolute, making the conditioned stronger in actualization. He supports this with a more precise reason from a Maghrebi investigator: it aligns better with the command to begin with the basmalah and praise, as the phrase explicitly indicates that the composition starts after that. Finally, he notes that 'wa-ba‘du' is used only when transitioning between types of discourse, and it is known as the 'virtue of speech' (fadl al-khitab), meaning the best part of speech, upon which scholars agree. This commentary is typical of the hashiya genre, expanding on the matn's wording to clarify grammar and rhetoric.

Key Terms
بعد
الظرف
معلَّق عليه
فضل الخطاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, why is the word 'ba‘du' in 'wa-ba‘du' mabni on damma?
A) Because it is a time adverb and all time adverbs are mabni.
B) Because the possessive noun is omitted and its meaning is intended, making it mabni like other noun phrases with omitted first term.
C) Because it is from the answer (jaza') of a condition, and answer expressions are mabni.
D) Because it is a proper noun for a specific moment.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'wa-ba‘du' is a key transition marker in classical Islamic texts; its grammatical form reflects nuanced rules about omitted noun phrases, and its rhetorical function is to elegantly move from preamble to subject.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find the phrase 'wa-ba‘du' in another classical Islamic text (e.g., the opening of a fiqh or kalam work). Identify its case (mabni or mansub) and explain why, based on whether the possessive noun is omitted in meaning or word.
?
Write a short sentence using 'wa-ba‘du' as a transition in a scholarly discussion, then explain its rhetorical function as fadl al-khitab.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Analyzing the Grammar of 'Ba'd' in Introductory Phrases
Grammatical and rhetorical analysis of 'ba'd' in the introductory phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible grammatical constructions of 'ba'd' in 'wa ba'd' and explain which is more famous and why.

Core Idea
The phrase 'wa ba'd' is a grammatical pivot that must be analyzed precisely to grasp the author's transition.

In classical Islamic texts, the phrase 'wa ba'd' (and after) signals a transition from the introduction to the main content. Its grammatical status affects how we understand the author's intent. In this passage from al-Bajuri's commentary, the author parses the possibilities: is 'ba'd' a noun with an omitted complement, or an adverb of time/place? And does it belong to the condition or the result clause? Mastering this analysis equips you to handle similar transitional phrases in any Arabic text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main constructions
Locate where the author says 'بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ حَذَفَ المُضَافَ إِلَيْهِ وَنَوَى مَعْنَاهُ' and 'بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ حَذَفَ المُضَافَ إِلَيْهِ وَنَوَى لَفْظَهُ'. Note that the first considers 'ba'd' as a noun with an omitted genitive complement (its meaning intended), and the second as an adverb in the accusative. The author says the first is 'الأَشْهَرُ' (more famous).
This highlights a common issue in Arabic: the same word can be parsed differently depending on the underlying assumption.
2
Classify 'ba'd' as temporal or spatial
The author gives examples: 'جَاءَ زَيْدٌ بَعْدَ عَمْرٍو' for time and 'دَارُ زَيْدٍ بَعْدَ دَارِ عَمْرٍو' for place. Determine which meaning applies here: the author says 'المُتَبَادَرُ هُنَا الأَوَّلُ' (the first is the more obvious). Why? Because the context of starting a book usually relates to temporal succession, though 'مكان الرقم' (place of the number) could also work.
This nuance is crucial when reading fiqh or kalam texts where time vs. place can change the ruling.
3
Decide whether 'wa ba'd' belongs to the condition or result
The phrase is part of an implied conditional sentence (e.g., 'ما بعد ذلك فكذا'). The author considers two probabilities: it may be from the operands of the condition (الشرط) or the result (الجزاء). He prefers the second because it makes the conditioned thing unconditional, which is more emphatic. Find the reasoning: 'لِيَكُونَ المُعَلَّقُ عَلَيْهِ مُطْلَقاً'.
This logical subtlety reflects a deeper concern for rhetorical strength in Islamic scholarly writing.
4
Understand the function as a transition marker
The author concludes by stating that this phrase is only used when transitioning from one type of discourse to another. The word is called 'فضل الخطاب' (surplus of discourse). This means it is a conventional tool, not carrying independent meaning, but structurally necessary.
Recognize that many Arabic scholarly texts use such formulas; knowing their grammar helps avoid misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ حَذَفَ المُضَافَ إِلَيْهِ وَنَوَى مَعْنَاهُ، وَيَصِحُ فِيهِ النَّصْبُ عَلَى الظَّرْفِيَّةِ؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ حَذَفَ المُضَافَ إِلَيْهِ وَنَوَى لَفْظَهُ، لَكِنَّ الأَشْهَرَ الأَوَّلُ. وَيُسْتَعْمَلُ هَذَا الطَّرْفُ لِلزَّمَانِ كَثِيراً؛ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكَ: جَاءَ زَيْدٌ بَعْدَ عَمْرٍو، وَلِلمَكَانِ قَلِيلاً؛ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكَ: دَارُ زَيْدٍ بَعْدَ دَارِ عَمْرٍو، وَالمُتَبَادَرُ هُنَا الأَوَّلُ، وَإِنْ صَحَ الثَّانِي أَيْضاً بِاعْتِبَارِ مَكَانِ الرَّقْمِ. وَهَلْ هُوَ مِنْ مَعْمُولَاتِ الشَّرْطِ، أَوْ مِنْ مَعْمُولَاتِ الجَزَاءِ احْتِمَالَانِ، وَالثَّانِي أَوْلَى؛ لِيَكُونَ المُعَلَّقُ عَلَيْهِ مُطْلَقاً، فَيَكُونَ المُعَلَّقُ أَقْوَى فِي التَّحَقُّقِ؛ لِأَنَّ المُعَلَّقَ عَلَى المُطْلَقِ أَبْلَغُ فِي التَّحَقُّقِ مِنَ المُعَلَّقِ عَلَى المُقَيِّدِ؛ كَذَا قَالُوا. وَالأَدَقُ فِي تَوْجِيهِ الأُولَوِيَّةِ مَا أَفَادَهُ بَعْضُ مُحَقِّقِي المَغَارِبَةِ مِنْ: أَنَّ ذَلِكَ أَمْثَلُ لِلأَمْرِ بِالبَدَاءَةِ بِالبَسْمَلَةِ وَمَا بَعْدَهَا المَفْهُومُ مِنَ الأَحَادِيثِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ صَرِيحٌ فِي أَنَّ الشُّرُوعَ فِي التَّأْلِيفِ بَعْدَ البَدَاءَةِ بِذَلِكَ، وَلَا كَذَلِكَ الأَوَّلُ. وَلَا يُؤْتَى بِهَذِهِ العِبَارَةِ إِلَّا عِنْدَ الانْتِقَالِ مِنْ نَوْعٍ مِنَ الكَلَامِ إِلَى نَوْعِ آخَرَ، وَهَذَا هُوَ مَعْنَى مَا اشْتُهِرَ مِنْ: أَنَّ هَذِهِ الكَلِمَةَ هِيَ فَضْلُ الخِطَابِ، كَمَا أَجْمَعَ عَلَيْهِ المُحَقِّقُونَ.
Based on the view that he omitted the genitive complement and intended its meaning, and it is permissible to put it in the accusative as an adverb of place; based on the view that he omitted the complement and intended its word, but the more famous is the first. This term is used frequently for time, as in your saying: 'Zayd came after Amr', and rarely for place, as in your saying: 'Zayd's house is after Amr's house'. The more common here is the first, even though the second is also correct considering the place of the number. There are two possibilities: is it part of the condition's operands or the result's operands? The second is preferable, so that the conditioned thing is unconditional, making the conditioned stronger in actuality; because the conditioned on the unconditional is more emphatic in actuality than the conditioned on the conditional. This is what they said. The more precise in justifying the preference is what some of the verifying scholars of the Maghrib provided: that this is more fitting for the command to begin with the Basmala and what follows it, which is understood from the hadiths; because it is explicit that the commencement of the composition is after beginning with that, and not so with the first. This phrase is only used when transitioning from one type of discourse to another, and this is the meaning of what is famous: that this word is the surplus of discourse, as the verifying scholars agreed.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and rhetorical analysis of the word 'ba'd' in the opening phrase 'wa ba'd'. The author discusses two main constructions: either 'ba'd' is construed as a noun with its genitive complement omitted but its meaning intended (so it is in the nominative of the subject), or it is construed as an adverb of time/place in the accusative. The more famous view is the first. Then the author explains that 'ba'd' is primarily used for temporal succession, with an example from daily speech, and occasionally for spatial succession. Here, the primary meaning is temporal, though spatial is possible if referring to the place of the text. Next, the author considers whether the phrase 'wa ba'd' belongs to the protasis (condition) or the apodosis (result) of the implied conditional sentence; the second option is preferred because it makes the conditioned thing unconditional, which is more emphatic. A more precise justification is given from Maghribi scholars: this construction better reflects the sunna of beginning with the Basmala, as the commencement of the composition after that is explicit. Finally, the author notes that 'wa ba'd' is used only as a transition marker, and it is considered 'fadl al-khitab' (surplus of speech) by consensus.

Key Terms
بعد
المضاف إليه
الظرفية
فضل الخطاب

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the more famous grammatical view of 'ba'd' in 'wa ba'd'?
A) It is an adverb of place in the accusative.
B) It is a noun with its genitive complement omitted but its meaning intended.
C) It is a particle with no grammatical function.
D) It is a verb in the past tense.

Key Takeaway
The grammatical analysis of 'ba'd' reveals that even a common transitional phrase carries multiple interpretive possibilities, and the more famous parsing often aligns with broader textual and religious considerations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find another transitional phrase in a classical text, e.g., 'fa-inna' in Ibn Hajar's 'Fath al-Bari'. Analyze its grammatical construction: Is it a particle, a noun, or something else? What function does it serve in the discourse?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Logic's Relation to the Heart like Grammar to the Tongue
Author introduces the benefit of logic and addresses a grammatical objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the analogy between logic and grammar as presented by the author and identify the benefit (thamara) of logic.

Core Idea
Logic protects the intellect just as grammar protects the tongue.

The opening line of this commentary establishes a powerful analogy: logic is to the heart (the seat of intellect) what grammar is to the tongue. This comparison highlights the function of logic as a tool that guards the mind from error in reasoning, much like grammar ensures correct speech. The author also hints at the 'fruit' (thamara) of logic, which is one of the ten essential principles that define a science. In this lesson, we will unpack this analogy and reflect on why logic is considered indispensable for Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core analogy
Find the two comparisons: logic is related to the heart (janan) and grammar to the tongue (lisan). Note that the heart here represents the intellect or inner faculty of reasoning.
The analogy is explicitly stated in the first line: 'Logic's relation to the heart is like grammar to the tongue.'
2
Explain what each part represents
Grammar provides rules for correct speech; logic provides rules for correct reasoning. Just as without grammar speech becomes chaotic and error-prone, without logic the intellect falls into confusion and false conclusions.
This shows that logic is not an alien discipline but a natural tool for preserving intellectual integrity.
3
Connect the analogy to the benefit (thamara)
The author says he indicated the fruit (thamara) of logic by this line. The fruit of a science is its practical benefit. For logic, the benefit is that it protects the mind from error in reasoning, which is essential for any systematic inquiry, especially in theology and jurisprudence.
The thamara is one of the ten principles of any science, as listed later in the passage.
4
Reflect on the grammatical objection and response
Read the commentary where an objection is raised about the conditional construction. The content of the result (the statement about logic) seems not to depend on a condition. The response clarifies that it is the act of informing that depends on the condition, not the content itself. This shows the precision with which scholars handled language.
This part demonstrates the close link between logic and grammar in the Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَبَعْدُ: فَالمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِ لِلَّسَانِ
الباجوري
قَوْلُهُ : (فَالمَنْطِقُ ... إلخ) أَيْ : «فَأَقُولُ : المَنْطِقُ ... إلخ ) 
فَانْدَفَعَ مَا يَرِدُ مِنْ : أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَضْمُونُ الجَزَاءِ مُرَتَّباً عَلَى فِعْل الشَّرْطِ . وَوَجْهُ الاِنْدِفَاعِ : أَنَّ مَضْمُونَ الجَزَاءِ فِي الحَقِيقَةِ الإِخْبَارُ بِالكَوْنِ المَذْكُورِ، لَا نَفْسُهُ، وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّهُ مُتَرَتِّبٌ عَلَى فِعْلِ الشَّرْطِ . نَعَمْ؛ يَرِدُ حِينَئِذٍ : أَنَّهُمْ نَضُوا عَلَى أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ حَذْفَ الفَاءِ» إذَا كَانَ المَحْذُوفُ قَوْلاً .
وَيُجَابُ بِأَنَّ هَذَا لَيْسَ مُتَّفَقاً عَلَيْهِ، بَلْ طَرِيقَةٌ لِبَعْضِهِمْ، فَيَكُونُ المُصَنِّفُ قَدْ جَرَى عَلَى الطَّرِيقَةِ الأُخْرَى القَائِلَةِ بِعَدَمِ وُجُوبِ حَذْفِ الفَاءِ حِينَئِذٍ ، كَمَا نَقَلَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ عَنْ هَمْعِ الهَوَامِعِ لِلسُّيُوطِيِّ . وَأَشَارَ المُصَنِّفُ بِهَذَا إِلَى ثَمَرَةِ هَذَا الفَنِّ الَّتِي هِيَ أَحَدُ المَبادِئ العَشَرَةِ المَنْظُومَةِ فِي قَوْلِ بَعْضِهِمْ : [من الرجز]
إِنَّ مَبَادِي كُلِّ فَنْ عَشَرَهُ الحَدُّ والمَوْضُوعُ ثُمَّ الثَّمَرَهُ وَفَضْلُهُ وَنِسْبَةٌ وَالوَاضِعْ وَالاسْمُ الاسْتِمْدَادُ حُكْمُ الشَّارِعُ مَسَائِلٌ وَالبَعْضُ بِالبَعْضِ اكْتَفَى وَمَنْ دَرَى الجَمِيعَ حَازَ الشَّرَفا
And after: Logic's relation to the heart is like grammar to the tongue. Al-Bajuri: His saying (So logic... etc.) meaning: 'So I say: Logic... etc.' Thus what is objected from that it is necessary that the content of the result be dependent on the action of the condition. And the face of repulsion: That the content of the result in reality is the informing of the mentioned state, not itself, and no doubt that it is dependent on the action of the condition. Yes; there arises then that they have stated that it is necessary to drop the 'fa' when the omitted is a saying. And it is answered that this is not agreed upon, but rather a method of some of them, so the author proceeded according to the other method that says there is no obligation to drop the 'fa' then, as some of them transmitted from Ham' al-Hawami' by al-Suyuti. And the author indicated by this the fruit of this art, which is one of the ten principles organized in the saying of some: [in rajaz] Indeed the principles of every art are ten: the definition, the subject, then the fruit, its virtue and relation, and the founder, the name, the derivation, the ruling of the Lawgiver, the issues. And some are satisfied with some, and whoever knows all has attained honor.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage opens the commentary on the poem's line. The line states that logic is to the heart (the intellect) as grammar is to the tongue. Al-Bajuri explains that the author is saying 'So I say: Logic...' and then addresses a grammatical objection: the result of a conditional sentence must depend on the condition. The objection is that here the result (the statement about logic) is not actually dependent on any condition. The answer is that the real result is the statement itself being made when the condition occurs, not the content. Then there is a further discussion about dropping the 'fa' in such constructions. The author, al-Bajuri, then notes that the poem's line indicates the benefit (thamar) of the science of logic, which is one of the ten principles of any art. He quotes a famous poem enumerating these ten principles: definition, subject, fruit, virtue, relation, founder, name, derivation, ruling of the Lawgiver, and issues. This sets the stage for the formal definition of logic.

Key Terms
المَنْطِق
الجَنَان
الثَّمَرَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the opening line, what is logic's relation to the heart compared to?
A) Grammar to the tongue
B) Grammar to the pen
C) Medicine to the body
D) Geometry to the mind

Key Takeaway
Logic is to the intellect as grammar is to speech: a protective tool that ensures correctness and prevents error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Write a short paragraph explaining how logic serves the heart (intellect) in the same way grammar serves the tongue in formulating correct arguments in fiqh. Use a concrete example, such as the ruling on riba.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Ten Principles of Any Science (al-Mabadi' al-Ashara)
Author lists the ten principles of any science, with emphasis on the fruit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten principles of a science as enumerated by al-Bajuri and explain the role of the 'fruit' (thamara) among them.

Core Idea
Every science is defined by ten foundational principles, including its definition, subject, and fruit.

In the commentary, after discussing the benefit of logic, al-Bajuri quotes a famous verse that lists the ten principles that constitute the foundation of any science. These principles are essential for understanding the scope and purpose of a discipline. This lesson will examine each of these ten elements, focusing on the 'fruit' (thamara) which represents the practical benefit of the science. By memorizing and applying these principles, students of knowledge can quickly grasp the structure of any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Extract the ten principles from the verse
Read the verse in the commentary: 'Indeed the principles of every art are ten: the definition, the subject, then the fruit, its virtue and relation, and the founder, the name, the derivation, the ruling of the Lawgiver, the issues.' List them in order.
The verse is in rajaz meter and is a common pedagogical tool.
2
Match each principle to its meaning
For each term, provide a brief explanation: the definition (hadd) clarifies what the science is; the subject (mawdu') is what it studies; the fruit (thamara) is its benefit; virtue and relation (fadl wa nisba) show its importance and connection to other sciences; the founder (wadi') is who established it; the name (ism) is its title; the derivation (ishtiqaq) shows the origin of its name; the ruling (hukm al-shari') indicates its legal status; and the issues (masa'il) are its specific topics.
Some sources combine some items, but here they are distinct.
3
Focus on the 'fruit' (thamara) as the benefit
The author specifically points to the 'fruit' of logic in the earlier line. The fruit is the practical result of studying the science. For logic, it is the ability to reason correctly. For other sciences, it is different. This principle reminds us that every science must have a tangible benefit.
The fruit is what motivates the study of a science.
4
Apply to an Islamic science
Choose a familiar Islamic science (e.g., usul al-fiqh) and try to identify its ten principles. For example, its subject is the evidence of fiqh, its fruit is the ability to derive rulings, etc. This helps internalize the structure.
Practicing this with different sciences builds a systematic understanding.

Source Text

الباجوري

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Subject of Logic
Definition of logic and its subject matter with restrictions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the subject matter of logic as conceptual and assent-based cognitions from the aspect of conveyance, and distinguish it from other aspects.

Core Idea
Logic is a tool that investigates cognitions only from the perspective of their ability to lead to unknown truths.

The definition of logic as a tool for the mind sets the stage, but its precise subject matter matters deeply. This lesson unpacks the complex definition of the subject of logic: conceptual and assent-based cognitions, but only from the aspect of their sound conveyance to the unknown. We will walk through the restrictions and essential accidents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of logic
Notice the analogy: logic is to the mind what grammar is to the tongue. This establishes logic as a normative tool for thinking.
The definition is descriptive (rasm), not real (hadd).
2
Extract the subject statement
The subject is 'al-ma'lumat al-tasawwuriyya wa al-tasdiqiyya' (conceptual and assent-based cognitions). This is the raw subject.
3
Note the restriction
The passage restricts the subject to 'from the aspect of sound conveyance' (min haythu sihhat al-isal). This excludes ontological or mental considerations.
The logician does not investigate whether cognitions exist, only whether they convey to the unknown.
4
Understand the dependency relationships
Proximate dependency: the syllogism depends on propositions. Remote dependency: propositions depend on concepts (subject and predicate). This hierarchy shows what the logician studies.
5
Recognize essential accidents
The essential accidents of the subject are conveyance and what depends on it (e.g., being a definition, proposition, categorical, conditional). The logician investigates these properties.
Essential accidents are those that belong to the subject due to its essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَبَعْدُ: فَالمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِ لِلِّسَانِ
الباجوري
- وَمَوْضُوعُهُ : المَعْلُومَاتُ التَّصَوُّرِيَّةُ وَالتَّصْدِيقِيَّةُ
الأنبابي
هذا؛ ثم ما سبق من كون الفصل أو الخاصة متوقفاً عليهما الموصل إذا لم يعرفا بكل منهما علی انفراده، فإن عرفا بكلِّ منهما على انفراده كانا من قبيل المعلومات التَّصوريَّة الموصلة بلا واسطة، والقواعد الباحثة عن المعلومات التصديقية المتوقف عليها الموصل للمجهول التصديقى توقُفاً قريباً القواعد المتعلّقة بالقضايا وأحكامها كالعكس ،والتناقض، وكونها حمليَّاتٍ أو شرطيَّاتٍ .
ووجه [ج/ ١٠] التَّوقف: أنَّ القياس الموصل للتصديق يتوقف على معرفة جزأيه، وهما: القضية الصُّغرى والكبرى، فلا بدَّ من معرفة القضيَّة بتعريفها وأحكامها والقواعد الباحثة عن المعلومات التصوريَّة، المتوقف عليها الموصل إلى التصديق توقُفاً بعيداً القواعد المتعلقة بالمحمول والموضوع، المذكورة في ضمن باب القضايا .
ووجه التَّوقُف : أنَّ القياس الموصل متوقف على القضيَّة التي هي جزؤه، والقضيَّة متوقفة على جزئها الذي هو المحمول أو الموضوع. فإن قيل : ليس في المنطق مسألة محمولها الإيصال أو ما يتوقف عليه الإيصال حتّى يقال: «علم يُبحث فيه عن المعلومات التَّصوريَّة والتصديقية من حيث إيصالها ... إلخ». قيل : إنَّ الحكم على المعلوم التَّصوري بأنه حد أو رسم معناه : أنَّه موصل إلى المجهول التصوري بلا واسطة، وقس على هذا .
ثمَّ إِنَّه قيَّد بقوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهَا تُوَصِّلُ ... إلخ) احترازاً عن البحث عنها، لا البحث عنها، لا من هذه الحيثيَّة ك كونها موجودة في الذهن، أو غير موجودة، وكونها ثابتة في نفس الأمر بقطع النظر عن اعتبار المعتبر. أو اعتباريَّةٌ محضة كـ : أنياب الأغوال، والقضايا الذهنية، فلا يبحث عنها المنطقي من هذه الجهات؛ إذ ليس غرضه متعلقاً بها . قوله : (وَمَوْضُوعُهُ : المَعْلُومَاتُ ... إلخ) أي : لأنَّ موضوع كلِّ علم ما يُبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية؛ أي: المنسوبة إلى ذات المعروض نسبةً قويَّةً كـ المعلومات المذكورة مِنَ الحيثية المذكورة، والأعراض الذاتية كـ: الإيصال، وما يتوقف عليه الإيصال كـ الجنسيَّة والفصلية وكونها قضيَّةً أو عكس قضيَّةٍ، وحمليّة أو شرطيَّة موجّهةً أو غير موجّهةٍ ؛ إذ هي المبحوث عنها في المنطق .
وإنَّما كان موضوع هذا الفنّ تلك المعلومات؛ لأنَّ المنطقي يبحث عن أحوالها التي هي الإيصال [ب/ ١٥]
(۱) في (ج) : «المجهول» بدلاً من «إلى المجهول»
الامم الناجون على السلم المرونق
(۹) وَبَعْدُ: فَالمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِ لِلِّسَانِ
الباجوري
(۱)
مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا إِلَى أَمْرٍ مَجْهُولٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِي (١). (۳) - وَثَمَرَتُهُ : مَا أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ المُصَنِّفُ مِنْ : أَنَّهُ يَعْصِمُ الذَّهْنَ عَنِ الخَطَأ فِي الفِكْرِ. وَقِيلَ: مَعْرِفَةُ التَّألِيفَاتِ الصَّحِيحَةِ وَالفَاسِدَةِ.
(٤) - وَفَضْلُهُ : فَوَقَانُهُ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ مِنَ العُلُومِ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ عَامَّ النَّفْعِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ يَبْحَثُ عَنْ كُلِّ عِلْمٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِيُّ (٢) ، وَهَذَا لَا يُنَافِي أَنَّ بَعْضَ بَاقِي العُلُومِ يَفُوقَهُ مِنْ حَيثَيَّةٍ أُخْرَى .
الأنبابي
(۲)
.
إلى المجهولات، وما يتوقَّفُ عليه هذا الإيصال، وهذه الأحوال هي العارضة للمعلومات التصورية والتصديقيَّة لذواتها، والفرق بين العوارض الذاتية وغيرها مذكور في القطب» و «حواشيه مع زياداتٍ أُخر متعلقة بالحد والموضوع المذكورين (۳).
قوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا ... إلخ) أي : فموضوع المنطق مقيَّد بصحة الإيصال، لا بنفس الإيصال؛ حتّى يرد عليه : أنَّ قيد الموضوع من تتمته، لا يُبحث عنه في العِلم ؛ إذ لا بدَّ في كلِّ علم من كون موضوعه مسلّم الثبوت، والإيصال مبحوث عنه في هذا العلم، فيجب أن يكون حالاً عارضةً للموضوع، لا مسلَّم الثبوت . ومحصّل الجواب : أنَّ قيد الموضوع هو صحة الإيصال، لا الإيصال نفسه، وعلى هذا القياس نظائر هذا القيد في موضوعات العلوم.
قوله : (وَقِيلَ : مَعْرِفَةُ التَّالِيفَاتِ... إلخ) في الحقيقة الثَّمرة الأولى متفرعة على هذه الثَّمرة .
(۱) الشرشيمي: قوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا ... إلخ) أي : المبحوث عنها من حيث صحة الإيصال، لا من حيث ذاتها، وكذلك ومِن حيث ما يتوقف عليه التّوصُّل، أو المعلومات كما تقدَّم، ولعله تركه لعلمه ممَّا سبق، أو اقتصاراً على المقصود. (۲) الشرشيمي: قوله : ( يَبْحَثُ عَنْ كُلِّ عِلْمٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِي) إن قلت : أيُّ علم تصوري؛ لأنَّ جميع العلوم تصديقات؟ : كل علم فيه تصور وتصديق، فإنَّ علم التوحيد مثلاً إذا قيل فيه: «القُدْرَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلهِ تَعَالَى، كان إدراك الطرفين تصوراً، وإدراك وقوع النسبة تصديقاً.
قلت :
ثمَّ ظهر أنَّ المراد بـ التَّصور» في العلوم: تصور تعاريف المفردات منها ؛ كـ تصور معنى الصَّلاة، والبيع، ... إلخ [1/ ١٤]، فإنَّ تعاريفها معلومات تصوريَّة توصل إلى أمر مجهول تصوري، وهو المعرّف، وأنَّ المراد بـ «التصديق» فيها : التصديق بالأقيسة الواقعة فيها ؛ كالقياس الحاصل في مقام الاستدلال على وجوب الصَّلاة بـ (أَقِيمُوا الصَّلوةَ ، فإنَّه يُقال : هذا أمر، وكلُّ أمرٍ للوجوب، وهكذا يقال في سائر الأدلة، وأما نفس الأحكام الفقهية كـ : كون فروض الوضوء ستَّة، أو كونه فرضاً، أو مندوباً ، فلا يُقال لها : معلومات تصوريَّة أو تصديقيَّة توصل ... إلخ» ؛ لأنَّها نفس المصدق بـ به، فهي نتيجة القياس والدليل، وإن كان إدراك مفرداتها تصوراً، وإدراك وقوع نسبتها تصديقاً؛ تأمل. (۳) انظر: مجموعة الشمسية) (١٥١/١) وما بعدها .
And after: Indeed, the relationship of logic to the mind is like that of grammar to the tongue. Al-Bajuri: And its subject matter: conceptual and assent-based cognitions. Al-Anbabi: This; then what preceded concerning the differentia or property being dependent on them, the conveyer, if they are not known by each of them individually; if they are known by each of them individually, they are of the category of conceptual cognitions conveying without mediation. And the rules investigating assent-based cognitions, upon which the conveyer to the unknown assent-based depends in a proximate dependency, are the rules related to propositions and their rulings like conversion and contradiction and their being categorical or conditional. And the aspect [vol. 10] of dependency: that the syllogism conveying to assent depends on knowledge of its two parts, which are the minor and major propositions, so knowledge of the proposition by its definition and rulings is necessary, and the rules investigating conceptual cognitions, upon which the conveyer to assent depends in a remote dependency, are the rules related to predicate and subject, mentioned within the chapter of propositions. And the aspect of dependency: that the conveying syllogism depends on the proposition which is its part, and the proposition depends on its part which is the predicate or subject. If it is said: There is no issue in logic whose predicate is conveyance or what depends on conveyance such that it is said: 'A science in which is investigated conceptual and assent-based cognitions from the aspect of their conveyance... etc.' It is said: Indeed, the judgment on the conceptual cognition that it is a definition or description means that it conveys to the unknown conceptual without mediation, and analogize to this. Then he restricted with his statement: 'From the aspect that they convey... etc.' as a precaution against investigating them not from this aspect, such as their being existent in the mind or not existent, and their being fixed in themselves regardless of consideration, or purely conventional like the tusks of ghouls and mental propositions, so the logician does not investigate them from these aspects, for his purpose is not related to them. His statement: 'And its subject matter: cognitions... etc.' means: because the subject of every science is that in which are investigated its essential accidentals; i.e., those attributed to the essence of the subject with a strong attribution like the mentioned cognitions from the mentioned aspect, and the essential accidentals like conveyance and what depends on conveyance like genericness and specificness and being a proposition or the converse of a proposition, and categorical or conditional, modal or non-modal; for they are what is investigated in logic. And the subject of this art is only those cognitions because the logician investigates their states which are conveyance [p. 15]. (1) In (j): 'the unknown' instead of 'to the unknown'. The successful nations on the luminous ladder (9) And after: Indeed, the relationship of logic to the mind is like that of grammar to the tongue. Al-Bajuri (1) From the aspect of soundness of its conveyance to an unknown conceptual or assent-based thing. (3) - And its fruit: what the author pointed to: that it safeguards the mind from error in thought. And it is said: knowledge of correct and corrupt compositions. (4) - And its virtue: its superiority over other sciences in terms of being general in benefit, because it investigates every conceptual and assent-based science (2), and this does not contradict that some of the remaining sciences surpass it from another aspect. Al-Anbabi (2). To the unknowns, and what this conveyance depends on, and these states are the accidentals that occur to conceptual and assent-based cognitions in themselves, and the difference between essential and non-essential accidentals is mentioned in al-Qutb and its glosses with other additions related to the definition and the mentioned subject (3). His statement: 'From the aspect of soundness of its conveyance... etc.' means: the subject of logic is restricted to soundness of conveyance, not to conveyance itself, to avoid objecting: that the restriction of the subject is part of its complement, it is not investigated in the science; for in every science its subject must be conceded existence, while conveyance is investigated in this science, so it must be an accidental state of the subject, not conceded existence. And the summary of the answer: that the restriction of the subject is soundness of conveyance, not conveyance itself, and analogize to this the parallels of this restriction in the subjects of the sciences. His statement: 'And it is said: knowledge of compositions... etc.' in reality the first fruit branches off from this fruit. (1) Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'From the aspect of soundness of its conveyance... etc.' means: those investigated from the aspect of soundness of conveyance, not from the aspect of themselves, and likewise from the aspect of what the conveyance depends on, or the cognitions as previously mentioned, and perhaps he left it due to his knowledge from what preceded, or confining to the intended. (2) Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'He investigates every conceptual or assent-based science.' If you say: Which conceptual science? For all sciences are assents? I say: Every science has conceptual and assent-based, for example in the science of tawhid if it is said: 'Power is necessary for Allah Almighty,' the apprehension of the two extremes is conceptual, and the apprehension of the occurrence of the relation is assent-based. Then it became clear that by 'conceptual' in the sciences is meant the conceptualization of definitions of its terms, like conceptualizing the meaning of prayer, sale, etc. [1/14], for their definitions are conceptual cognitions that convey to an unknown conceptual thing, which is the definiendum, and by 'assent-based' in them is meant the assent to the syllogisms occurring in them, like the syllogism in the context of deducing the obligation of prayer by 'Establish prayer', for it is said: This is a command, and every command is for obligation, and similarly for all evidences. As for the actual jurisprudential rulings like the obligatory acts of ablution being six, or being obligatory, or recommended, they are not called conceptual or assent-based cognitions that convey... etc., because they are themselves the [object of] assent, so they are the result of the syllogism and evidence, although apprehending their terms is conceptual and apprehending the occurrence of their relation is assent-based; reflect. (3) See: Majmu'at al-Shamsiyya (1/151) and after.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is an excerpt from a commentary on al-Sullam, opening the discussion of logic (mantiq). It proceeds in a structured manner: first, a definition of logic by analogy, then its subject matter, fruit, and virtue. The commentator al-Anbabi expands on each point. The opening line likens logic's role for the mind to grammar's role for the tongue, establishing logic as a tool for correct thinking. The subject matter (mawdu') is then declared: conceptual (tasawwuri) and assent-based (tasdiqi) cognitions, but with a crucial qualification—only from the perspective of their ability to convey (isal) to unknown cognitions. The commentator justifies this by explaining the proximate and remote dependencies of syllogisms on propositions and their parts. He defends the definition against a potential objection: that 'conveyance' is not a predicate of any logical issue. He then clarifies the restriction 'from the aspect that they convey' to exclude investigations of cognitions from other aspects (e.g., existence, mental existence). The discussion of essential accidentals (arad dhatiyya) follows, enumerating what the logician investigates: conveyance and its prerequisites. The fruit (thamara) is twofold: safeguarding the mind from error, and knowledge of correct and corrupt compositions; the first branches from the second. The virtue (fadl) is its universal benefit, since it investigates all sciences, though some sciences may surpass it in other respects. Marginal notes from al-Shirshimi further clarify the meaning of 'from the aspect of soundness' and explain how 'conceptualization' and 'assent' apply within the sciences, using examples from fiqh (prayer, sale) and usul al-fiqh (command and obligation). The commentary thus systematically unpacks the matn lines, providing foundational definitions that set the scope of logic.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the subject matter of logic?
A) All cognitions regardless of aspect.
B) Conceptual and assent-based cognitions from the aspect of their sound conveyance.
C) Only propositions and their conversions.
D) The mind and its faculties.

Key Takeaway
Logic investigates conceptual and assent-based cognitions exclusively from the perspective of their ability to lead soundly to unknown cognitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a conceptual cognition in fiqh (e.g., 'salah') and explain how it conveys to an unknown conceptual thing (its definition).
?
List the essential accidents that a logician investigates about this cognition according to the passage.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Fruit and Virtue of Logic
Fruit and virtue of logic with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the twofold fruit of logic (safeguarding the mind and distinguishing correct from corrupted compositions) and its universal benefit across all sciences.

Core Idea
Logic safeguards the mind from error and benefits every science, though it does not surpass them in their own domains.

Having defined logic and its subject, the tradition turns to why we study it: its fruit (thamara) and its virtue (fadl). The fruit is practical: it protects the mind from error in thought. The virtue is its universal applicability. This lesson unpacks these end goals and their implications for the student of Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two statements of the fruit
First: 'it safeguards the mind from error in thought.' Second: 'knowledge of correct and corrupt compositions.' Note that these are related.
2
Understand the relationship between the fruits
Al-Anbabi states that the first fruit (safeguarding) branches from the second (knowledge of compositions). You cannot safeguard the mind without knowing what correct reasoning looks like.
3
Identify the virtue
Logic is superior (fawaq) to other sciences in being 'general in benefit' (amm al-naf‘). It investigates all sciences from the aspect of their conceptual and assent-based cognitions.
4
Recognize the caveat
Other sciences may surpass logic in other aspects (e.g., their specific subject matter). Logic's superiority is only in generality, not in everything.
5
Apply the marginal note
Al-Shirshimi explains how 'conceptual' and 'assent-based' apply in sciences: conceptual refers to definitions of terms (e.g., prayer, sale), and assent-based refers to syllogisms (e.g., command implies obligation). This shows the universal scope.

وَبَعْدُ: فَالمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِ لِلِّسَانِ
الباجوري
- وَمَوْضُوعُهُ : المَعْلُومَاتُ التَّصَوُّرِيَّةُ وَالتَّصْدِيقِيَّةُ
الأنبابي
هذا؛ ثم ما سبق من كون الفصل أو الخاصة متوقفاً عليهما الموصل إذا لم يعرفا بكل منهما علی انفراده، فإن عرفا بكلِّ منهما على انفراده كانا من قبيل المعلومات التَّصوريَّة الموصلة بلا واسطة، والقواعد الباحثة عن المعلومات التصديقية المتوقف عليها الموصل للمجهول التصديقى توقُفاً قريباً القواعد المتعلّقة بالقضايا وأحكامها كالعكس ،والتناقض، وكونها حمليَّاتٍ أو شرطيَّاتٍ .
ووجه [ج/ ١٠] التَّوقف: أنَّ القياس الموصل للتصديق يتوقف على معرفة جزأيه، وهما: القضية الصُّغرى والكبرى، فلا بدَّ من معرفة القضيَّة بتعريفها وأحكامها والقواعد الباحثة عن المعلومات التصوريَّة، المتوقف عليها الموصل إلى التصديق توقُفاً بعيداً القواعد المتعلقة بالمحمول والموضوع، المذكورة في ضمن باب القضايا .
ووجه التَّوقُف : أنَّ القياس الموصل متوقف على القضيَّة التي هي جزؤه، والقضيَّة متوقفة على جزئها الذي هو المحمول أو الموضوع. فإن قيل : ليس في المنطق مسألة محمولها الإيصال أو ما يتوقف عليه الإيصال حتّى يقال: «علم يُبحث فيه عن المعلومات التَّصوريَّة والتصديقية من حيث إيصالها ... إلخ». قيل : إنَّ الحكم على المعلوم التَّصوري بأنه حد أو رسم معناه : أنَّه موصل إلى المجهول التصوري بلا واسطة، وقس على هذا .
ثمَّ إِنَّه قيَّد بقوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهَا تُوَصِّلُ ... إلخ) احترازاً عن البحث عنها، لا البحث عنها، لا من هذه الحيثيَّة ك كونها موجودة في الذهن، أو غير موجودة، وكونها ثابتة في نفس الأمر بقطع النظر عن اعتبار المعتبر. أو اعتباريَّةٌ محضة كـ : أنياب الأغوال، والقضايا الذهنية، فلا يبحث عنها المنطقي من هذه الجهات؛ إذ ليس غرضه متعلقاً بها . قوله : (وَمَوْضُوعُهُ : المَعْلُومَاتُ ... إلخ) أي : لأنَّ موضوع كلِّ علم ما يُبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية؛ أي: المنسوبة إلى ذات المعروض نسبةً قويَّةً كـ المعلومات المذكورة مِنَ الحيثية المذكورة، والأعراض الذاتية كـ: الإيصال، وما يتوقف عليه الإيصال كـ الجنسيَّة والفصلية وكونها قضيَّةً أو عكس قضيَّةٍ، وحمليّة أو شرطيَّة موجّهةً أو غير موجّهةٍ ؛ إذ هي المبحوث عنها في المنطق .
وإنَّما كان موضوع هذا الفنّ تلك المعلومات؛ لأنَّ المنطقي يبحث عن أحوالها التي هي الإيصال [ب/ ١٥]
(۱) في (ج) : «المجهول» بدلاً من «إلى المجهول»
الامم الناجون على السلم المرونق
(۹) وَبَعْدُ: فَالمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِ لِلِّسَانِ
الباجوري
(۱)
مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا إِلَى أَمْرٍ مَجْهُولٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِي (١). (۳) - وَثَمَرَتُهُ : مَا أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ المُصَنِّفُ مِنْ : أَنَّهُ يَعْصِمُ الذَّهْنَ عَنِ الخَطَأ فِي الفِكْرِ. وَقِيلَ: مَعْرِفَةُ التَّألِيفَاتِ الصَّحِيحَةِ وَالفَاسِدَةِ.
(٤) - وَفَضْلُهُ : فَوَقَانُهُ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ مِنَ العُلُومِ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ عَامَّ النَّفْعِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ يَبْحَثُ عَنْ كُلِّ عِلْمٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِيُّ (٢) ، وَهَذَا لَا يُنَافِي أَنَّ بَعْضَ بَاقِي العُلُومِ يَفُوقَهُ مِنْ حَيثَيَّةٍ أُخْرَى .
الأنبابي
(۲)
.
إلى المجهولات، وما يتوقَّفُ عليه هذا الإيصال، وهذه الأحوال هي العارضة للمعلومات التصورية والتصديقيَّة لذواتها، والفرق بين العوارض الذاتية وغيرها مذكور في القطب» و «حواشيه مع زياداتٍ أُخر متعلقة بالحد والموضوع المذكورين (۳).
قوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا ... إلخ) أي : فموضوع المنطق مقيَّد بصحة الإيصال، لا بنفس الإيصال؛ حتّى يرد عليه : أنَّ قيد الموضوع من تتمته، لا يُبحث عنه في العِلم ؛ إذ لا بدَّ في كلِّ علم من كون موضوعه مسلّم الثبوت، والإيصال مبحوث عنه في هذا العلم، فيجب أن يكون حالاً عارضةً للموضوع، لا مسلَّم الثبوت . ومحصّل الجواب : أنَّ قيد الموضوع هو صحة الإيصال، لا الإيصال نفسه، وعلى هذا القياس نظائر هذا القيد في موضوعات العلوم.
قوله : (وَقِيلَ : مَعْرِفَةُ التَّالِيفَاتِ... إلخ) في الحقيقة الثَّمرة الأولى متفرعة على هذه الثَّمرة .
(۱) الشرشيمي: قوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا ... إلخ) أي : المبحوث عنها من حيث صحة الإيصال، لا من حيث ذاتها، وكذلك ومِن حيث ما يتوقف عليه التّوصُّل، أو المعلومات كما تقدَّم، ولعله تركه لعلمه ممَّا سبق، أو اقتصاراً على المقصود. (۲) الشرشيمي: قوله : ( يَبْحَثُ عَنْ كُلِّ عِلْمٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِي) إن قلت : أيُّ علم تصوري؛ لأنَّ جميع العلوم تصديقات؟ : كل علم فيه تصور وتصديق، فإنَّ علم التوحيد مثلاً إذا قيل فيه: «القُدْرَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلهِ تَعَالَى، كان إدراك الطرفين تصوراً، وإدراك وقوع النسبة تصديقاً.
قلت :
ثمَّ ظهر أنَّ المراد بـ التَّصور» في العلوم: تصور تعاريف المفردات منها ؛ كـ تصور معنى الصَّلاة، والبيع، ... إلخ [1/ ١٤]، فإنَّ تعاريفها معلومات تصوريَّة توصل إلى أمر مجهول تصوري، وهو المعرّف، وأنَّ المراد بـ «التصديق» فيها : التصديق بالأقيسة الواقعة فيها ؛ كالقياس الحاصل في مقام الاستدلال على وجوب الصَّلاة بـ (أَقِيمُوا الصَّلوةَ ، فإنَّه يُقال : هذا أمر، وكلُّ أمرٍ للوجوب، وهكذا يقال في سائر الأدلة، وأما نفس الأحكام الفقهية كـ : كون فروض الوضوء ستَّة، أو كونه فرضاً، أو مندوباً ، فلا يُقال لها : معلومات تصوريَّة أو تصديقيَّة توصل ... إلخ» ؛ لأنَّها نفس المصدق بـ به، فهي نتيجة القياس والدليل، وإن كان إدراك مفرداتها تصوراً، وإدراك وقوع نسبتها تصديقاً؛ تأمل. (۳) انظر: مجموعة الشمسية) (١٥١/١) وما بعدها .
And after: Indeed, the relationship of logic to the mind is like that of grammar to the tongue. Al-Bajuri: And its subject matter: conceptual and assent-based cognitions. Al-Anbabi: This; then what preceded concerning the differentia or property being dependent on them, the conveyer, if they are not known by each of them individually; if they are known by each of them individually, they are of the category of conceptual cognitions conveying without mediation. And the rules investigating assent-based cognitions, upon which the conveyer to the unknown assent-based depends in a proximate dependency, are the rules related to propositions and their rulings like conversion and contradiction and their being categorical or conditional. And the aspect [vol. 10] of dependency: that the syllogism conveying to assent depends on knowledge of its two parts, which are the minor and major propositions, so knowledge of the proposition by its definition and rulings is necessary, and the rules investigating conceptual cognitions, upon which the conveyer to assent depends in a remote dependency, are the rules related to predicate and subject, mentioned within the chapter of propositions. And the aspect of dependency: that the conveying syllogism depends on the proposition which is its part, and the proposition depends on its part which is the predicate or subject. If it is said: There is no issue in logic whose predicate is conveyance or what depends on conveyance such that it is said: 'A science in which is investigated conceptual and assent-based cognitions from the aspect of their conveyance... etc.' It is said: Indeed, the judgment on the conceptual cognition that it is a definition or description means that it conveys to the unknown conceptual without mediation, and analogize to this. Then he restricted with his statement: 'From the aspect that they convey... etc.' as a precaution against investigating them not from this aspect, such as their being existent in the mind or not existent, and their being fixed in themselves regardless of consideration, or purely conventional like the tusks of ghouls and mental propositions, so the logician does not investigate them from these aspects, for his purpose is not related to them. His statement: 'And its subject matter: cognitions... etc.' means: because the subject of every science is that in which are investigated its essential accidentals; i.e., those attributed to the essence of the subject with a strong attribution like the mentioned cognitions from the mentioned aspect, and the essential accidentals like conveyance and what depends on conveyance like genericness and specificness and being a proposition or the converse of a proposition, and categorical or conditional, modal or non-modal; for they are what is investigated in logic. And the subject of this art is only those cognitions because the logician investigates their states which are conveyance [p. 15]. (1) In (j): 'the unknown' instead of 'to the unknown'. The successful nations on the luminous ladder (9) And after: Indeed, the relationship of logic to the mind is like that of grammar to the tongue. Al-Bajuri (1) From the aspect of soundness of its conveyance to an unknown conceptual or assent-based thing. (3) - And its fruit: what the author pointed to: that it safeguards the mind from error in thought. And it is said: knowledge of correct and corrupt compositions. (4) - And its virtue: its superiority over other sciences in terms of being general in benefit, because it investigates every conceptual and assent-based science (2), and this does not contradict that some of the remaining sciences surpass it from another aspect. Al-Anbabi (2). To the unknowns, and what this conveyance depends on, and these states are the accidentals that occur to conceptual and assent-based cognitions in themselves, and the difference between essential and non-essential accidentals is mentioned in al-Qutb and its glosses with other additions related to the definition and the mentioned subject (3). His statement: 'From the aspect of soundness of its conveyance... etc.' means: the subject of logic is restricted to soundness of conveyance, not to conveyance itself, to avoid objecting: that the restriction of the subject is part of its complement, it is not investigated in the science; for in every science its subject must be conceded existence, while conveyance is investigated in this science, so it must be an accidental state of the subject, not conceded existence. And the summary of the answer: that the restriction of the subject is soundness of conveyance, not conveyance itself, and analogize to this the parallels of this restriction in the subjects of the sciences. His statement: 'And it is said: knowledge of compositions... etc.' in reality the first fruit branches off from this fruit. (1) Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'From the aspect of soundness of its conveyance... etc.' means: those investigated from the aspect of soundness of conveyance, not from the aspect of themselves, and likewise from the aspect of what the conveyance depends on, or the cognitions as previously mentioned, and perhaps he left it due to his knowledge from what preceded, or confining to the intended. (2) Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'He investigates every conceptual or assent-based science.' If you say: Which conceptual science? For all sciences are assents? I say: Every science has conceptual and assent-based, for example in the science of tawhid if it is said: 'Power is necessary for Allah Almighty,' the apprehension of the two extremes is conceptual, and the apprehension of the occurrence of the relation is assent-based. Then it became clear that by 'conceptual' in the sciences is meant the conceptualization of definitions of its terms, like conceptualizing the meaning of prayer, sale, etc. [1/14], for their definitions are conceptual cognitions that convey to an unknown conceptual thing, which is the definiendum, and by 'assent-based' in them is meant the assent to the syllogisms occurring in them, like the syllogism in the context of deducing the obligation of prayer by 'Establish prayer', for it is said: This is a command, and every command is for obligation, and similarly for all evidences. As for the actual jurisprudential rulings like the obligatory acts of ablution being six, or being obligatory, or recommended, they are not called conceptual or assent-based cognitions that convey... etc., because they are themselves the [object of] assent, so they are the result of the syllogism and evidence, although apprehending their terms is conceptual and apprehending the occurrence of their relation is assent-based; reflect. (3) See: Majmu'at al-Shamsiyya (1/151) and after.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is an excerpt from a commentary on al-Sullam, opening the discussion of logic (mantiq). It proceeds in a structured manner: first, a definition of logic by analogy, then its subject matter, fruit, and virtue. The commentator al-Anbabi expands on each point. The opening line likens logic's role for the mind to grammar's role for the tongue, establishing logic as a tool for correct thinking. The subject matter (mawdu') is then declared: conceptual (tasawwuri) and assent-based (tasdiqi) cognitions, but with a crucial qualification—only from the perspective of their ability to convey (isal) to unknown cognitions. The commentator justifies this by explaining the proximate and remote dependencies of syllogisms on propositions and their parts. He defends the definition against a potential objection: that 'conveyance' is not a predicate of any logical issue. He then clarifies the restriction 'from the aspect that they convey' to exclude investigations of cognitions from other aspects (e.g., existence, mental existence). The discussion of essential accidentals (arad dhatiyya) follows, enumerating what the logician investigates: conveyance and its prerequisites. The fruit (thamara) is twofold: safeguarding the mind from error, and knowledge of correct and corrupt compositions; the first branches from the second. The virtue (fadl) is its universal benefit, since it investigates all sciences, though some sciences may surpass it in other respects. Marginal notes from al-Shirshimi further clarify the meaning of 'from the aspect of soundness' and explain how 'conceptualization' and 'assent' apply within the sciences, using examples from fiqh (prayer, sale) and usul al-fiqh (command and obligation). The commentary thus systematically unpacks the matn lines, providing foundational definitions that set the scope of logic.

The fruit of logic is twofold: practical protection from error and the epistemic ability to distinguish valid from invalid reasoning, while its virtue lies in its universal utility across all sciences.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Logic's Distinctness from Other Sciences
Author states logic's distinctness from sciences in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why logic is distinct from other sciences in definition but universal in subject.

Core Idea
Logic is distinct not in subject but in form—it measures every science without being one.

The passage opens by stating that logic's relation to the sciences is its distinctness from them (mubayana). But then the commentary clarifies that this distinctness is only in definition (hadd), because its subject—conceptual and assensual information—is common to all sciences. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase 'mubayanatuhu laha'
Find where the author says logic is distinct from sciences. This is the key claim.
2
Contrast definition vs subject
Al-Shirshimi explains that the distinctness is in definition, not subject. What is the subject of logic? How does it include all sciences?
The universal subject is 'tasawwurat wa tasdiqat'.
3
Apply to a real science
Consider how logic applies to usul al-fiqh. Does logic itself study the same objects as usul? Why or why not?

Introduction of the poet: Its relation to the sciences is its distinctness from them. (9) After this: the relation of logic to the mind is like that of grammar to the tongue. Al-Bajuri: (5) And its relation to the sciences is its distinctness from them. (6) And its founder: 'Aristu' – with kasra on the hamza, fatha on the ra and sin, and damma on the ta, and he is Aristotle, contrary to those who imagined that they are two persons. (7) And its name: 'al-mantiq' as the author mentioned, and it is also called 'al-mizan' (the balance), and 'mi'yar al-ulum' (the standard of sciences). And it is only named 'al-mantiq' because 'mantiq' originally applies to: perception, and to the rational faculty, and to speech which is utterance. And this art – by it perception increases and becomes correct, and by it the rational faculty becomes strong and complete, and by it becomes the ability for speech. So since it has a connection to each of these three meanings, it was named by that. Al-Anbabi: His words: 'and bi: mi'yar al-ulum' meaning: the balance of perceptions by which one knows the correct from the corrupt. His words: 'applies to perception' – and from it is 'natiq' in the definition of man; i.e., one who perceives universal perception; i.e., much. And by 'universal' is excluded the perception of other animals, so they are not called 'mantiq' or 'nutq'. And it is on this a verbal noun (masdar mimi), as it is on the third meaning similarly, contrary to the second meaning, for it is a noun of place. His words: 'and to the rational faculty' i.e., that which is the locus of issuing those perceptions. His words: 'by it increases' – it is said: the fronting of the object in the three places is for emphasis, not for restriction; for other than logic also has a role, although it is more involved. His words: 'the ability' i.e., complete ability. (1) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'its distinctness from them' i.e., with respect to definition; but with respect to its subject it is general to every science, because your statement 'conceptual and assensual information' includes every science as clarified previously. (2) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'and he is Aristotle' – he abbreviated from it: 'Aristu'. (3) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'applies to perception' – on this and on the third it is a verbal noun (masdar mimi), and on the second it is a noun of place. (4) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'by it perception increases ... etc.' – explanation: by it the rational faculty through which perception occurs becomes strong, so perception increases at that point, and then he becomes able to utter speech; because it only happens after perception and deliberation of meanings, so it is a metaphor originally from the category of applying the name of a thing whose description is caused by another thing to that other thing. (5) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'and by it the ability' – fronting of the prepositional phrase is for emphasis, not restriction; because other than it also produces that, and the aspect of emphasis is that it is more beneficial than other things in that.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage continues the introduction to logic by addressing three points: its relation to other sciences, its founder, and its names. The opening matn line repeats the analogy with grammar. Al-Bajuri explains that logic is distinct from other sciences in its definition (hadd), but its subject matter – conceptual and assensual information – is universal to all sciences, as clarified by the commentary of al-Shirshimi. The founder is Aristotle (إرسط or إرسطاطاليس), and the text corrects the misconception that 'Aristu' and 'Aristotalis' refer to two different persons. The names of logic include 'al-mantiq' (logic), 'al-mizan' (the balance), and 'mi'yar al-ulum' (the standard of sciences). The name 'mantiq' is motivated by its connection to three meanings of 'nutq': perception (idrak), the rational faculty (al-quwwa al-'aqila), and speech (al-nutq as utterance). Logic increases perception and makes it accurate, strengthens the rational faculty, and enables proper articulation of ideas. Thus, it is appropriately named after these functions. Al-Anbabi comments on 'mi'yar al-ulum' as the balance of perceptions distinguishing correct from incorrect. He also explains that 'natiq' in the definition of man ('animal natiq') means 'perceiving universal perception', excluding animals. The verbal noun forms are clarified: for the first and third meanings it is a masdar mimi, for the second a noun of place. The fronting of objects in the phrases 'by it perception increases' etc. is for emphasis, not restriction, because other factors also contribute. Al-Shirshimi adds that logic's relation to sciences is distinct in definition but its subject covers all sciences, and confirms the abbreviation of Aristotle's name. The explanation of the metaphor: logic causes the strengthening of the rational faculty, so it is called by the name of its effect.

التصورات والتصديقات

The Founder of Logic: Aristotle
Author identifies Aristotle as founder and rejects the idea of two persons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the founder of logic and refute the misconception of two Aristotles.

Core Idea
The founder of logic is one person: Aristotle; 'Aristu' is an abbreviation, not a different individual.

The matn attributes logic to Aristotle (إرسط), and immediately clarifies that this is the same as Aristotle (إرسطاطاليس). Some mistakenly thought they were two different individuals. This lesson examines that correction.

Guided Path
1
Locate the founder's name
Find the name 'إرسط' and the full name 'إرسطاطاليس' in the Arabic. Note the spelling difference.
2
Understand the misconception
The text says 'خلافاً لمن توهم أنهما شخصان'. What was the misconception? Why might it arise?
3
View the commentary
Al-Shirshimi says 'فاختصر منه: أرسيط' – the shorter name is an abbreviation. How does that resolve the issue?

(( وَإِنَّمَا سُمِّيَ بـ : المَنْطِقِ»؛ لِأَنَّ المَنْطِقَ فِي الأَصْلِ يُطْلَقُ عَلَى : الإِدْرَاكِ) ، وَعَلَى : القُوَّةِ العَاقِلَةِ، وَعَلَى : النُّطْقِ الَّذِي هُوَ التَّلَفُظُ، وَهَذَا الفَنُّ بِهِ يَكْثُرُ الإِدْرَاكُ وَيُصِيبُ (٤) ، وَبِهِ تَتَقَوَى القُوَّةُ العَاقِلَةُ وَتَكْمُلُ، وَبِهِ تَكُونُ القُدْرَةُ عَلَى النُّطْقِ ، فَلَمَّا كَانَ لَهُ ارْتِبَاطُ بِكُلِّ مِنْ هَذِهِ المَعَانِي الثَّلَاثَةِ سُمِّيَ بِذَلِكَ . (٥) الأنبابي قوله : (وَبِ: مِعْيَارِ العُلُومِ») أي : ميزان الإدراكات الذي يعرف به صحيحها من فاسدها [1/ ١٠]. قوله : (يُطْلَقُ عَلَى : الإِدْرَاكِ) ومنه نَاطِقٌ» في تعريف الإِنْسَان»؛ أي: مُدْرِك إدراكاً كليا ؛ أي: كثيراً . وخرج بـ «كُلّيّا»: إدراك غير الإنسان مِنَ الحَيَوَانات، فلا يسمى: «منطقاً» و: «نطقاً»، وهو على هذا مصدر ميمي، كما هو على الإطلاق الثَّالث كذلك، بخلافه على الثاني، فإنَّه اسم مكان. قوله : (وَعَلَى : القُوَّةِ العَاقِلَةِ أي التي هي محل صدور تلك الإدراكات. : قوله : (بِهِ يَكْثُرُ) قيل : تقديم المعمول في المواضع الثَّلاثة؛ للاهتمام، لا للحصر؛ إذ لغير المنطق دخل أيضاً، وإن كان هو أدخل . قوله : (تَكُونُ القُدْرَةُ) أي: التَّامَّة . (۱) الشرشيمي : قوله : (مُبَايَنَتُهُ لَهَا ) أي : بالنظر للحد، وأمَّا بالنظر لموضوعه فهو عام لكلِّ علم؛ لأنَّ قولك : المعلومات التصوريَّة والتصديقيَّة» يشمل : كل علم كما تقدَّم توضيحه (۲) الشرشيمي : قوله : (وَهُوَ إِرَسْطَاطَالِيسُ) فاختصر منه : «أرسيط». (۳) الشرشيمي : قوله : (يُطْلَقُ عَلَى : الإِدْرَاكِ وعلى هذا وعلى الثَّالث يكون مصدراً ميميا ، وعلى الثاني يكون اسم مكان. (٤) الشرشيمي : وقوله : (بِهِ يَكْثُرُ الإِدْرَاكُ ... إلخ) توضيح ذلك : أنَّ به تتقوى القوَّة العاقلة التي بها الإدراك، فيكثر الإدراك عند ذلك، فيقدر على التلفظ ؛ لأنَّه لا يكون إلا بعد الإدراك والتَّدبر للمعاني، فهو مجاز بحسب الأصل من باب إطلاق اسم الشَّيء الذي تسبب وصفه عن شيء آخر على ذلك الشَّيء الآخر . (5) الشرشيمي : وقوله : (وَبِهِ تَكُونُ القُدْرَةُ) تقديم الجار والمجرور ؛ للاهتمام، لا للحصر ؛ لأنَّ غيره يحصل منه ذلك أيضاً، ووجه الاهتمام : أنَّه أنفع من غيره في ذلك.
Introduction of the poet: Its relation to the sciences is its distinctness from them. (9) After this: the relation of logic to the mind is like that of grammar to the tongue. Al-Bajuri: (5) And its relation to the sciences is its distinctness from them. (6) And its founder: 'Aristu' – with kasra on the hamza, fatha on the ra and sin, and damma on the ta, and he is Aristotle, contrary to those who imagined that they are two persons. (7) And its name: 'al-mantiq' as the author mentioned, and it is also called 'al-mizan' (the balance), and 'mi'yar al-ulum' (the standard of sciences). And it is only named 'al-mantiq' because 'mantiq' originally applies to: perception, and to the rational faculty, and to speech which is utterance. And this art – by it perception increases and becomes correct, and by it the rational faculty becomes strong and complete, and by it becomes the ability for speech. So since it has a connection to each of these three meanings, it was named by that. Al-Anbabi: His words: 'and bi: mi'yar al-ulum' meaning: the balance of perceptions by which one knows the correct from the corrupt. His words: 'applies to perception' – and from it is 'natiq' in the definition of man; i.e., one who perceives universal perception; i.e., much. And by 'universal' is excluded the perception of other animals, so they are not called 'mantiq' or 'nutq'. And it is on this a verbal noun (masdar mimi), as it is on the third meaning similarly, contrary to the second meaning, for it is a noun of place. His words: 'and to the rational faculty' i.e., that which is the locus of issuing those perceptions. His words: 'by it increases' – it is said: the fronting of the object in the three places is for emphasis, not for restriction; for other than logic also has a role, although it is more involved. His words: 'the ability' i.e., complete ability. (1) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'its distinctness from them' i.e., with respect to definition; but with respect to its subject it is general to every science, because your statement 'conceptual and assensual information' includes every science as clarified previously. (2) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'and he is Aristotle' – he abbreviated from it: 'Aristu'. (3) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'applies to perception' – on this and on the third it is a verbal noun (masdar mimi), and on the second it is a noun of place. (4) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'by it perception increases ... etc.' – explanation: by it the rational faculty through which perception occurs becomes strong, so perception increases at that point, and then he becomes able to utter speech; because it only happens after perception and deliberation of meanings, so it is a metaphor originally from the category of applying the name of a thing whose description is caused by another thing to that other thing. (5) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'and by it the ability' – fronting of the prepositional phrase is for emphasis, not restriction; because other than it also produces that, and the aspect of emphasis is that it is more beneficial than other things in that.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage continues the introduction to logic by addressing three points: its relation to other sciences, its founder, and its names. The opening matn line repeats the analogy with grammar. Al-Bajuri explains that logic is distinct from other sciences in its definition (hadd), but its subject matter – conceptual and assensual information – is universal to all sciences, as clarified by the commentary of al-Shirshimi. The founder is Aristotle (إرسط or إرسطاطاليس), and the text corrects the misconception that 'Aristu' and 'Aristotalis' refer to two different persons. The names of logic include 'al-mantiq' (logic), 'al-mizan' (the balance), and 'mi'yar al-ulum' (the standard of sciences). The name 'mantiq' is motivated by its connection to three meanings of 'nutq': perception (idrak), the rational faculty (al-quwwa al-'aqila), and speech (al-nutq as utterance). Logic increases perception and makes it accurate, strengthens the rational faculty, and enables proper articulation of ideas. Thus, it is appropriately named after these functions. Al-Anbabi comments on 'mi'yar al-ulum' as the balance of perceptions distinguishing correct from incorrect. He also explains that 'natiq' in the definition of man ('animal natiq') means 'perceiving universal perception', excluding animals. The verbal noun forms are clarified: for the first and third meanings it is a masdar mimi, for the second a noun of place. The fronting of objects in the phrases 'by it perception increases' etc. is for emphasis, not restriction, because other factors also contribute. Al-Shirshimi adds that logic's relation to sciences is distinct in definition but its subject covers all sciences, and confirms the abbreviation of Aristotle's name. The explanation of the metaphor: logic causes the strengthening of the rational faculty, so it is called by the name of its effect.

Key Terms
إِرَسَط
إِرَسْطَاطَالِيس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the relationship between 'Irasat' and 'Irastatalis'?
A) They are two different logicians
B) They are the same person with the latter being an abbreviation
C) They are both students of Plato
D) They are the same person but Irasat is the Arabic version

Key Takeaway
Aristotle is the sole founder of logic; the two names refer to the same figure.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Search for references to 'Aristu' and 'Aristotalis' in Islamic philosophical texts. Determine if they are used interchangeably and whether the distinction matters for the argument being made.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Why Logic is Called al-Mantiq
Author explains why logic is called al-mantiq based on three meanings of the root.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three meanings of nutq and how logic relates to each.

Core Idea
Logic is called mantiq because it perfects perception, strengthens the rational faculty, and enables coherent speech.

The passage gives three meanings of the root 'n-t-q': perception, rational faculty, and speech. Logic is named after these because it enhances all three. This lesson breaks down each connection.

Guided Path
1
List the three meanings
Find in the Arabic the three meanings: الإدراك, القوة العاقلة, النطق (التلفظ). Write them down.
2
Explain each connection
For each meaning, the text states how logic improves it: perception increases and becomes correct, rational faculty becomes strong, ability for speech becomes complete. Why does logic do that?
3
Note the commentary on emphasis
Al-Anbabi notes that the fronted phrases are for emphasis (if itrab) not restriction (if hasr). Why is it important that logic is not the sole cause?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Defining Key Terms in Logic's Praise
Al-Bajuri defines terms and explains metaphor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the terminological definition of fikr and distinguish between ghaiy and khata based on al-Bajuri's commentary.

Core Idea
Logic elevates thought from mere movement to precise reasoning and distinguishes types of error.

Al-Bajuri unpacks a poetic line that extols logic. He gives precise technical meanings to the terms used, showing that logic is not just any thinking but a structured method that avoids error and uncovers deep understanding.

Guided Path
1
Examine the definitions of 'fikr'
Read the Arabic: fikr linguistically is 'movement of the soul among intelligibles'; terminologically it is 'arrangement of two known things to reach an unknown'. Note the shift from general to specific.
2
Distinguish between 'ghaiy' and 'khata'
Ghaiy is error in general (opposite of guidance). Khata can be defined in three ways: error due to forgetfulness, deliberate error, or absolute error. Understand the idafa relation between them.
The idafa can be general-specific or appositional.
3
Analyze the metaphor of uncovering
The line says logic 'uncovers the covering from subtle understanding'. Al-Bajuri explains this as a metaphor (isti'ara): understanding is like a covered object, logic removes the cover.
This shows that logic reveals what is otherwise hidden.

وَقَوْلُهُ : ((الأَفْكَارَ جَمْعُ: «فِكْرِ» وَهُوَ كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ : حَرَكَةُ النَّفْسِ فِي المَعْقُولَاتِ لُغَةٌ، وَ: «تَرْتِيبُ أَمْرَيْنِ (١) مَعْلُومَيْنِ لِيُتَوَصَّلُ بِهِمَا إِلَى أَمْرٍ مَجْهُولٍ اصْطِلاحاً . وَقَوْلُهُ : (عَنْ غَيّ الخَطَا مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِقَوْلِهِ : يَعْصِمُ، وَالغَيُّ : الصَّلَالُ، وَهُوَ ضِدُّ الهُدَى؛ كَمَا فِي القَامُوسِ وَغَيْرِهِ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ عَنْ عَمْدٍ أَوْ عَنْ سَهْرٍ . وَالخَطَأ : «الصَّلَالُ إِذَا كَانَ عَنْ سَهْرٍ، وَقِيلَ: «إِذَا كَانَ عَنْ عَمْدٍ، وَقِيلَ: «مُطْلَقاً»، فَفِيهِ ثَلَاثَةُ أَقْوَالٍ حَكَاهَا صَاحِبُ «القَامُوسِ» (٢) . فَعَلَى الأَوَّلَيْنِ تَكُونُ إِضَافَةِ الغَيِّ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ العَامُ لِلخَاصٌ كَمَا فِي: «شَجَرُ أَرَاكِ»، المُسَمَّاةُ عِنْدَهُمْ بِالإِضَافَةِ الَّتِي لِلبَيَانِ، وَأَمَّا عَلَى الأَخِيرِ (٣) فَهِيَ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ أَحَدِ المُتَرَادِفَيْنِ لِلآخَرِ، فَسَقَطَ مَا لِبَعْضِهِمْ هُنَا . قَوْلُهُ : : (وَعَنْ دَقِيقِ الفَهم ... إلخ) «الوَاوُ دَاخِلَةٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ : يَكْشِفُ، وَالإِضَافَةُ فِي قَوْلِهِ : دَقِيقِ الفَهْمِ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ الصَّفَةِ لِلمَوْصُوفِ وَالفَهُمُ بِمَعْنَى المَفْهُومِ، وَالتَّقْدِيرُ حِينَئِذٍ : وَيَكْشِفُ الغِطَاءَ عَنِ المَفْهُومِ الدَّقِيقِ . وَفِي كَلَامِهِ اسْتِعَارَةٌ بِالكِنَايَةِ وَتَخْيِيلُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ شَبَّهَ دَقِيقَ الفَهْمِ بِشَيْءٍ مُغَطَّى تَشْبِيها مُضْمَراً فِي النَّفْسِ، وَحَذَفَ اسْمَ المُشَبِّهِ بِهِ، وَأَثْبَتَ شَيْئاً مِنْ لَوَازِمِهِ تَحْيِيلاً وَهُوَ الغِطَاءُ، وَالكَشْفُ تَرْشِيحُ . إِنْ كَانَ حَقِيقَةٌ فِي الحِرِّيَّاتِ فَقَط كَمَا مَرَّ ، وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ الغِطَاءَ بِكَسْرِ الغَيْنِ المُعْجَمَةِ : السِّتْرُ - بِكَسْرِ السِّيْنِ المُهْمَلَةِ ، وَأَمَّا بِفَتْحِهَا فَالمَصْدَرُ .
And his statement: 'al-afkar' is the plural of 'fikr' which, as previously mentioned, is linguistically the movement of the soul among intelligibles, and terminologically the arrangement of two known things to reach an unknown thing through them. And his statement: 'an ghaiy al-khata' is connected to his statement: 'ya'simu', and 'al-ghaiy' is error, the opposite of guidance, as in al-Qamus and others, whether deliberate or due to forgetfulness. And 'al-khata' is error if due to forgetfulness, and it is said if deliberate, and it is said absolutely. There are three statements related by the author of al-Qamus. According to the first two, the idafa of ghaiy to it is the idafa of the general to the specific, like 'shajaru araki', called by them the idafa of elucidation. As for the last, it is the idafa of one of two synonyms to the other, so what some have said here falls away. His statement: 'wa 'an daqiq al-fahm ... etc.' The waw enters on his statement: 'yakshifu', and the idafa in his statement 'daqiq al-fahm' is the idafa of the adjective to the described, and 'al-fahm' is in the sense of 'al-mafhum', so the estimation then is: 'and he uncovers the covering from the subtle concept'. And in his speech there is a metaphorical allusion and imagery, because he has likened subtle understanding to something covered, a simile implicit in the mind, and he removed the name of the likened thing, and established something of its concomitants as imagery, namely the covering, and the uncovering is the ratification. If it is literal only in the free women as previously, and it is not hidden that 'al-ghita'' with a kasra of the ghayn is the veil with a kasra of the sin, and with a fatha it is the verbal noun.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a commentary by al-Bajuri on a line of poetry praising logic. He first defines 'afkar' (thoughts) as the plural of 'fikr', which has two meanings: linguistic (movement of the soul among intelligibles) and terminological (arrangement of two known things to reach an unknown). He then explains the phrase 'an ghaiy al-khata' (from the error of mistake). He defines 'ghaiy' as error, the opposite of guidance, whether deliberate or accidental. He notes that 'khata' specifically means error due to forgetfulness, according to one opinion, or deliberate according to another, or absolute. He discusses the grammatical idafa (construct phrase) between 'ghaiy' and 'khata': if they are different, it is a general-specific relation; if synonymous, it is an apposition. He then addresses 'daqiq al-fahm' (subtle understanding), parsing it as an adjectival idafa, meaning 'subtle concept' (al-mafhum al-daqiq). He identifies a metaphor (isti'ara) in the line: understanding is compared to something covered, and the verb 'yakshifu' (uncovers) is used, with 'al-ghita' (the covering) as the image. Finally, he clarifies the vocalization of 'ghita': with kasra on the ghayn, it means veil; with fatha, it is the verbal noun. Thus, logic protects the mind from all error and unveils deep comprehension.

?

(Answer: This is khata, because it is due to forgetfulness; it is also ghaiy as a general error.)
