خاتمة
(۱۳۰) نَظَمَهُ العَبْدُ الدَّلِيلُ المُفْتَقِرُ لِرَحْمَةِ المَوْلَى العَظِيمِ المُقْتَدِرُ (۱۳۱) الأَخْضَرِيُّ عَابِدُ الرَّحْمَنِ المُرْتَجِيْ مِنْ رَبِّهِ المَنَّـانِ (۱۳۲) مَغْفِرَةٌ تُحِيْطُ بالذُّنُوبِ وَتَكْشِفُ الغِطَاعَنِ القُلُوبِ
الباجوري
وَ المَوْلَى يُطْلَقُ عَلَى مَعَانٍ كَثِيرَةٍ مِنْهَا : الحَلِيفُ ، وَالنَّاصِرُ ، وَالحَلِيمُ الَّذِي لَا يَسْتَفِرُّهُ الغَضَبُ . قَوْلُهُ : (العَظِيْمِ) أَيْ : عَظَمَةٌ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ، لَا حِرِّيَّةٌ؛ لِاسْتِحَالَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى، فَإِنَّهَا تَسْتَدْعِي الجِسْمِيَّةَ. قَوْلُهُ : (المُقْتَدِرْ) هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِنَ القَادِرِ » ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى المُقْتَدِرِ »: تَامُ القُدْرَةِ، وَمَعْنَى القَادِرِ» : المُتَّصِفُ بِالقُدْرَةِ، وَيَصِحُ هُنَا أَنْ يُقَالَ : لِأَنَّ زِيَادَةَ البِنَاءِ تَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ المَعْنَى؛ لاتِّحَادِ نَوْعِ الكَلِمَتَيْنِ المَذْكُورَتَيْنِ، فَإِنَّهُمَا اسْمَا فَاعِلِ.
قَوْلُهُ : (الأَخْضَرِيُّ) نِسْبَةٌ لِـ «الأَخْضَر جَبَلْ بِالمَغْرِبِ عَلَى مَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُ المَغَارِبَةِ.
وَهَذَا بَيَانُ لِنِسْبَتِهِ بِحَسَبِ مَا اشْتُهِرَ عَلَى الأَلْسِنَةِ، وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلعَبَّاسِ بْنِ مِرْدَاسَ الصَّحَابِيِّ المَشْهُورِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ المُصَنِّفُ فِي شَرْحِهِ . قَوْلُهُ : (عَابِدُ الرَّحْمَنِ) إِنَّمَا زَادَ الأَلِفَ فِي ذَلِكَ لِلوَزْنِ، وَإِلَّا فَاسْمُهُ: «عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ»، وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنَّ المُصَنِّفَ لَمْ يُرِدِ العَلَمَ . قَوْلُهُ : (المُرْتَجِيْ أَي : المُؤَمِّلَ مَعَ الأَخْذِ فِي الأَسْبَابِ كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا مَرَّ، وَمَعْمُولُ قَوْلِهِ : المُرْتَجِيْ مَا ذَكَرَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ : «مَغْفِرَةٌ تُحِيطُ ... إلخ » ، وَقَوْلِهِ : وَإِنْ يُبَنَا ... إلخ». قَوْلُهُ : ( مِنْ رَبِّهِ المَنَّانِ) أَيْ : كَثِيرِ المَنِّ ؛ الَّذِي هُوَ الإِنْعَامِ، أَوْ تَعْدَادُ النِّعَمِ ، وَهُوَ بِالمَعْنَى الثَّانِي مَذْمُومٌ ؛ إِلَّا بِالنِّسْبَةِ اللهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ، وَاسْتَتَنى بَعْضُهُمُ الشَّيْخَ وَالوَالِدَ . قَوْلُهُ : (مَغْفِرَةٌ) مَأخُوذَةٌ مِنَ الغَفْرِ وَهُوَ : السِّتْرُ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهَا : سِتْرُ الذُّنُوبِ عَنْ أَعْيُنِ المَلَائِكَةِ قِيلَ : مَعَ كَوْنِهَا بَاقِيَةٌ فِي الصَّحِيفَةِ، لَكِنْ لَا يُؤَاخِذُ بِهَا صَاحِبُهَا، وَقِيلَ: مَعَ مَحْوِهَا مِنَ الصَّحِيفَةِ مِنْ أَصْلِهَا .
قَوْلُهُ : (تُحِيْطُ بالذُّنُوبِ كِنَايَةٌ عَنْ كَوْنِهَا تَعُمُّ جَمِيعَهَا بِحَيْثُ لَا يَبْقَى فَرْدٌ مِنْهَا .
مَغْفِرَةٌ تُحِيطُ بالذُّنُوبِ وَتَكْشِفُ الغِطَا عَنِ القُلُوبِ (۱۳۳) وَأَنْ يُثِيْبَنَا بِجَنَّةِ العُلَى فَإِنَّهُ أَكْرَمُ مَنْ تَفَضَّلَا (١٣٤) وَكُنْ أَخِي لِلْمُبْتَدِي مُسَامِحَا وَكُنْ لإِصْلَاحِ الفَسَادِ نَاصِحَا
الباجوري
قَوْلُهُ : (وَتَكْشِفُ الغِطَا عَنِ القُلُوبِ) أَيْ : تُزِيلُ الحِجَابَ المُحْدِقَ بِالقُلُوبِ، الحَائِلَ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ عَلَّامِ الغُيُوبِ، الحَاصِلَ بِسَبَبِ اقْتِرَافِ الذُّنُوبِ عَنْ تِلْكَ القُلُوبِ ).
وَفِي الكَلَام اسْتِعَارَةٌ بِالكِنَايَةِ، فَيَكُونُ المُصَنِّفُ قَدْ شَبَّهَ القُلُوبَ بِأَشْيَاءَ لَهَا غِطَاءُ، وَطَوَى لَفْظَ المُشَبَّهَ بِهِ وَرَمَزَ إِلَيْهِ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ لَوَازِمِهِ وَهُوَ الغِطَاءُ . وَيَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ فِيهِ اسْتِعَارَةٌ تَصْرِيحِيَّةٌ، فَيَكُونُ قَدْ شَبَّهَ مَا يَحْصُلُ عَلَى القُلُوبِ بِسَبَبِ الذُّنُوبِ بِالغِطَاء؛ بِجَامِعِ : المَنْعِ فِي كُلِّ، وَاسْتَعَارَ لَفْظَ المُشَبَّهَ بِهِ لِلْمُشَبَّهِ، وَعَلَى كُلِّ فَالكَشْفُ تَرْشِيحُ إِنْ كَانَ حَقِيقَةٌ فِي الحِرِّيَّاتِ فَقَط كَمَا مرَّ .
قَوْلُهُ : (وَأَنْ يُثِيْبَنَا) قَدْ عَرَفْتَ أَنَّهُ مَعْطُوفٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ : «مَغْفِرَةٌ تُحِيطُ ... إلخ».
وَقَوْلُهُ : (بِجَنَّةِ العُلَى) أَيْ : بِجَنَّةِ الدَّرَجَاتِ العُلَى، فَـ «العُلَى» : صِفَةٌ لِمَوْصُوفٍ مَحْذُوفٍ، كَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ، وَهُوَ أَوْلَى مِنْ قَوْلِ بَعْضِهِمْ : أَنَّهُ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ المَوْصُوفِ لِلصِّفَةِ، وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ «العُلَى جَمْعُ: «عُلْيَا» - بِضَمِّ العَيْنِ مَعَ القَصْرِ ؛ بِمَعْنَى : العَلْيَاء» - بِفَتْحِ العَيْنِ مَعَ المَد .. قَوْلُهُ : (فَإِنَّهُ أَكْرَمُ مَنْ تَفَضَّلَا) عِلَّةٌ لِقَوْلِهِ : «المُرْتَجِي ... إلخ»، وَهَذَا يَقْتَضِي أَنَّ لِغَيْرِهِ تَعَالَى تَفَضُّلا وَكَرَماً ، وَهُوَ كَذَلِكَ بِحَسَبِ الظَّاهِرِ، وَأَمَّا بِحَسَبِ الحَقِيقَةِ فَلَيْسَ التَّفَضُلُ وَالكَرَمُ إِلَّا لَهُ تَعَالَى، فَكَلَامُ المُصَنِّفِ بِالنَّظَرِ لِلظَّاهِرِ ؛ كَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ .
قَوْلُهُ : (وَكُنْ أَخِي) أَيْ: فِي الإِسْلَامِ.
وَقَوْلُهُ: لِلْمُبْتَدِي مُسَامِحَا) أَيْ: مِنَ الزَّلَلِ الَّذِي قَدْ يَظْهَرُ فِي هَذَا التَّألِيفِ، وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ أنَّ «المُبْتَدِي» هُوَ : الآخِذُ فِي صِغَارِ العِلْمِ، وَلَا يَخْفَى مَا فِي ذَلِكَ وَمَا بَعْدَهُ مِنْ تَوَاضُعِ المُصَنِّفِ؛ حَيْثُ جَعَلَ نَفْسَهُ مُبْتَدِنَا وَلَمْ يَأْمَنْ مِنْ وُقُوعِ الزَّلَلِ فِي تَألِيفِهِ.
Conclusion. (130) Composed it the servant, the humble, the needy for the mercy of the Master, the Mighty, the All-Powerful. (131) Al-Akhdari, worshipper of the Most Merciful, hoping from his Lord, the Bestower, (132) for forgiveness that encompasses sins and removes the veil from hearts. Al-Bajuri: And 'al-Mawla' is applied to many meanings, among them: the ally, the helper, the forbearing one whom anger does not incite. His saying: 'al-'Azim' meaning: a meaningful greatness, not physical, because it is impossible for Him, Exalted, for that would entail corporeality. His saying: 'al-Muqtadir' is more eloquent than 'al-Qadir', because the meaning of 'al-Muqtadir' is perfect in power, and the meaning of 'al-Qadir' is the one described with power. And here it is correct to say: because the increase in form indicates an increase in meaning, due to the agreement of the type of the two mentioned words, for they are both active participles. His saying: 'al-Akhdari' is a nisba to 'al-Akhdar', a mountain in the Maghrib, as some Maghribis said. And this is an explanation of his lineage according to what is well-known in speech; otherwise, he is attributed to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, the famous Companion, as the author said in his commentary. His saying: 'Abid al-Rahman' — he only added the alif in that for meter; otherwise his name is 'Abd al-Rahman', and it is possible that the author did not intend the proper name. His saying: 'al-Murtaji' meaning: the one hoping while taking the means, as is known from what has passed, and the object of his saying 'al-Murtaji' is what he mentioned by his saying 'forgiveness that encompasses ... etc.' and his saying 'and that He reward us ... etc.' His saying: 'from his Lord, al-Mannan' meaning: abundant in favor, which is bestowal, or counting of blessings, and in the second sense it is blameworthy except with respect to Allah and His Messenger, and some exempted the teacher and the father. His saying: 'maghfira' is derived from 'ghafr' which is: covering, and what is meant by it is: the covering of sins from the eyes of the angels. It is said: while they remain in the record, but its owner is not taken to account for them; and it is said: with their erasure from the record entirely. His saying: 'encompasses sins' is a metonymy for it including all of them such that no individual of them remains. Forgiveness that encompasses sins and removes the veil from hearts (133) and that He reward us with the Garden of the Most High, for He is the most generous of those who bestow favor (134) and be a brother to the beginner, lenient, and be for the correction of corruption an adviser. Al-Bajuri: His saying: 'and removes the veil from hearts' meaning: it removes the veil surrounding the hearts, preventing between them and the Knower of the Unseen, resulting from committing sins from those hearts. And in the speech there is a metaphor by metonymy, so the author likened the hearts to things that have a veil, and he omitted the word of the thing likened and signaled to it by one of its necessities, namely the veil. And it is valid that there is an explicit metaphor in it, so he likened what occurs to the hearts due to sins to a veil, with the common factor of prevention in each, and he borrowed the word of the thing likened to for the thing likened. In any case, 'removal' is a reinforcement if it is real only in physical entities as previously mentioned. His saying: 'and that He reward us' — you know that it is coordinate to his saying 'forgiveness that encompasses ... etc.' And his saying: 'with the Garden of the Most High' meaning: with the Garden of the highest ranks. So 'al-'ula' is an adjective for a deleted described thing, as some investigators said, and it is preferable to what some said: that it is from the annexation of the described to the adjective. And it is not hidden that 'al-'ula' is the plural of 'ulya' — with damm of the 'ayn and with qasr, meaning 'al-'alya' — with fatha of the 'ayn and with madd. His saying: 'for He is the most generous of those who bestow favor' is a cause for his saying 'al-murtaji ... etc.', and this requires that others besides Him, Exalted, have generosity and kindness, and that is so in appearance, but in reality there is no generosity and kindness except for Him, Exalted. So the author's speech is with consideration of the outward, as some said. His saying: 'and be a brother' meaning: in Islam. And his saying: 'to the beginner lenient' meaning: concerning the slips that may appear in this composition. It has already passed that 'al-mubtadi' is the one taking up the rudiments of knowledge. And it is not hidden what is in that and after it of the author's humility, where he made himself a beginner and did not feel safe from the occurrence of slips in his composition.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is the commentary (sharh) by al-Bajuri on the final lines (khātima) of the matn 'al-Sullam al-Murawniq' by al-Akhdari. The commentary explains each phrase of the poetic conclusion. The passage begins with the matn lines in parentheses (numbered 130-134), followed by al-Bajuri's explanatory notes.

First, al-Bajuri clarifies the term 'al-Mawla' (the Master) used in line 130, noting its multiple meanings: ally, helper, forbearing one. Then he addresses 'al-'Azim' (the Mighty), emphasizing that God's greatness is not physical but qualitative, as physicality is impossible for God. Next, he distinguishes 'al-Muqtadir' (the All-Powerful) from 'al-Qadir' (the Powerful), explaining that the form 'mufta'il' indicates perfection of the attribute, and that in Arabic, increased form often signifies increased meaning.

He then explains the nisba 'al-Akhdari', mentioning two possible derivations: from a mountain named 'al-Akhdar' in the Maghrib, or from the Companion al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas. He notes that the poet added an alif in 'Abid al-Rahman' for metrical reasons, as the usual form is 'Abd al-Rahman'.

The commentary proceeds to define 'al-murtaji' (the one hoping) as one who hopes while taking the means, and 'al-Mannan' (the Bestower) as the one who grants favors, distinguishing between the praiseworthy giving of blessings and the blameworthy counting of them (except by Allah and His Messenger).

Regarding 'maghfira' (forgiveness), he explains it as covering sins from the angels' eyes, with two opinions on whether the sins remain in the record or are erased entirely. The phrase 'encompasses sins' is a metonymy indicating that forgiveness covers all sins.

Moving to page 356, al-Bajuri explains 'removes the veil from hearts' as removing the barrier caused by sins that prevents hearts from perceiving the Knower of the Unseen. He provides a detailed rhetorical analysis, identifying either a metaphor by metonymy (where a necessary concomitant 'veil' replaces the object 'hearts') or an explicit metaphor (where the state of sin is likened to a veil).

Then he clarifies that 'and that He reward us' is co-ordinate to the earlier request for forgiveness. He explains 'the Garden of the Most High' as the Garden of the highest ranks, analyzing 'al-'ula' as a plural adjective or as an instance of the described being added to its attribute.

The 'cause' in 'for He is the most generous of those who bestow favor' is connected to the earlier supplication; though generosity appears to apply to others, in reality it belongs only to God.

Finally, the commentator explains the last couplet: 'be a brother' means in Islam, and 'to the beginner lenient' refers to being tolerant of errors in this composition. He notes the author's humility in calling himself a beginner and admitting the possibility of mistakes.

Every explanation follows the order of the matn lines and provides linguistic, theological, or rhetorical depth.

Key Terms
المُبْتَدِي
مُسَامِحَا
نَاصِحَا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, what does the author request regarding the 'beginner' (al-mubtadi)?
A) To teach him strictly and correct every mistake harshly.
B) To be lenient with him and advise for correction.
C) To ignore his errors and focus on advanced students.
D) To consider him an equal and debate with him.

Key Takeaway
The closing of the Sullam models the virtue of humility and the duty to guide others gently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Write a brief response (in the style of a teacher) to a student who has made a mistake in formulating a syllogism, using the advice from the khatima: be lenient and an adviser for correction.
?

Reading a Logical Commentary's Title Page
This passage identifies the title and author of the commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, commentary title, and base text from a classical logical commentary's title page.

Core Idea
Title pages are the birth certificate of Islamic texts—they fix authorship and lineage.

Every scholarly work in the Islamic tradition opens with a title page that establishes its identity. For students of logic, being able to read these pages is essential for situating a text within its intellectual lineage. This lesson examines the title page of al-Bannani's commentary on al-Sullam al-Murawniq, one of the most studied didactic poems on logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentary indicator
Look for the word 'Sharh' (شح/شرح) at the beginning. It signals that this work is a commentary expanding upon a base text.
In corrupted OCR, 'شح' may appear instead of 'شرح'.
2
Identify the commentary's own title
The next phrase is the title of the commentary itself. Here it is 'al-Umm al-Thanai' (الأمم الثنائى). This is the name by which scholars refer to this particular commentary.
The exact reading is uncertain due to OCR; a scholar may verify.
3
Identify the base text (matn)
The word 'ala' (علا/على) means 'upon', and the following name 'al-Sullam al-Murawniq' is the base text being commented on. This is a famous didactic poem on logic.
4
Identify the author and his death date
The word 'Ta'lif' (تأليف) introduces the author. The full name and death year (1194 AH) are given. This establishes the author's identity and era, key for historical contextualization.
Death dates help date the work and assess its influence.

Title page and author attribution of the commentary.

Core Idea
The Luminous Ladder: A step-by-step guide to logic by al-Akhdari, explained by al-Bannani.

This lesson introduces the foundational text of Islamic logic, al-Sullam al-Murawniq, and its commentary by Imam al-Bannani. Understanding the authorship and title of this work is crucial for situating subsequent logical discussions within the broader Islamic scholarly tradition.

Guided Path

Identify the title
The title is 'السلم المرونق' (al-Sullam al-Murawniq), meaning 'The Luminous Ladder'. This is the commentary, not the original poem.
The original poem is also called al-Sullam al-Murawniq; the commentary is a hashiya (super-commentary).

The author of this commentary is الإمام محمد بن الحسن بن مسعود البناني (Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Mas'ud al-Bannani).
Al-Bannani is a prominent logician from the 12th/18th century.

This commentary is part of the Bajuri-Bannani tradition, building upon al-Akhdari's original matn and its earlier sharh. It is a key text in the study of Islamic logic.
Knowing the author and title helps you locate the text within the broader curriculum.

Understanding the Role of a Gloss (Taqyeed) in Islamic Scholarship
The glossator praises al-Bannani's commentary and introduces his own gloss.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key rhetorical and functional components of a glossator's introduction and explain the relationship between a gloss (taqyeed) and its base commentary.

Core Idea
A gloss does not merely repeat—it unveils hidden meanings and refines understanding.

This passage is the introduction of a glossator (muhashshi) writing a super-commentary on al-Bannani's Sharh al-Sullam. It combines praise of Allah, eulogy of the Prophet, and commendation of the base commentary, while stating the need for further explanation. Such introductions are a standard feature in Islamic scholarly works, especially in logic and other disciplines, where each layer of commentary aims to clarify the previous one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three-part structure
Look for the typical opening: praise of Allah (hamdalah), salutation on the Prophet (salawat), and the transition phrase 'amma ba'd' (to proceed). This structure frames the scholarly work within a devotional context.
In this passage, the hamdalah emphasizes Allah's role in creating genera of subjects and predicates.
2
Examine the description of the Prophet's logic
The Prophet is described as 'possessor of eloquent and lucid logic' (mantiq fasih baligh). Note how this links his speech to the clarity of Sharia definitions.
This highlights that logic (mantiq) is not alien to Islamic revelation; the Prophet exemplified it.
3
Analyze the praise of al-Bannani's commentary
The glossator highlights qualities: brevity (ijaz), solidity (ihkam al-mabani), refinement (tahrir al-taqawwul), and clarification (tanqih al-ma'ani). These are criteria for a good commentary.
The commentary is said to make difficult concepts accessible and to apply restrictions where needed.
4
Understand the glossator's justification
Despite the commentary's excellence, its 'brides are veiled' – deeper meanings require further explanation. The glossator's role is to unveil them, justifying his own work.
This shows that glosses are not mere reproductions but interpretive expansions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنَّ أنفسَ ما سُكِّر في الطُّرُوس من تصوُّرٍ أو تصديق، وأبلغ حجّةٍ تُرشد لنتائج التحقيق، حمد الله عن الكلِّ والجزء والتّركيب والتَّلفيق المنفرد بإيجاد أجناس الموضوعات ومحمولاتها من غير شرط في ذلك ولا تعليق والصَّلاة والسَّلامُ على سيدنا محمَّدٍ صاحب المنطق الفصيح البليغ، الآتي بحدود الشَّريعة والمبيِّن لرسومها بأتم تبليغ، وعلى آله وأصحابه مطالع أنواره الشَّمسيَّة، المصدقين لرسالته العامة المطلقة الكلية؛ أما بعد: فهذه تقاييد تتشوّف لعرائس خدورها الأذهان، وتقارير تتشرف بسماع مبانيها الآذان، موضوعةٌ على شرح السُّلَّم» للإمام الرَّبَّاني، الحائز قصب السبق في استخراج فرائد الفوائد من بحر المعاني، أبي عبد الله سيدي محمد بن الحسن البناني - أسكنه الله تعالى بفضله ومنه دارَ التّهانى، فيا له من شرح جمع بين الإيجاز وإحكام المباني، وتحرير التقول وتنقيح المعاني، يُقرب للأفهام ما كان شموساً شموعاً، ويُقيّد المطلق ويطلق ما كان تقييده ممنوعاً، بيد أنَّ عرائسه محجبَةٌ في الخدور، تفتقر في الاطلاع عليها لمن يكشف عنها السُّتور.
Indeed, the most precious of what is written on pages of conceptualizations or assents, and the most compelling proof that guides to the results of verification, is praise of Allah for the whole and the part, composition and arrangement, the Unique in creating the genera of subjects and predicates without condition or qualification. And prayers and peace upon our master Muhammad, possessor of eloquent and lucid logic, who brought the limits of the Sharia and explained its definitions with complete conveyance, and upon his family and companions, the rising places of his solar lights, who attest to his universal, absolute, and general message. To proceed: These are notes that long for the brides of their minds in seclusion, and reports honored by ears listening to their structures, composed upon the commentary on 'al-Sullam' by the spiritual Imam, the one who has won the race in extracting unique benefits from the ocean of meanings, Abu Abdullah Sayyidi Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Bannani – may Allah the Exalted, by His bounty and grace, give him an abode in the abode of delight. What a commentary it is – it combines brevity and solidity of structure, refinement of expression and clarification of meanings. It brings close to minds what was as elusive as wild suns, and it restricts the unrestricted and releases what was forbidden to restrict. Yet its brides are veiled in seclusions, needing someone to unveil them.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is the glossator's introduction (muqaddimat al-muhashshi). It opens with a rhetorical flourish praising the highest type of knowledge – that which is recorded on pages, be it conceptualizations (tasawwur) or assents (tasdiq), and the best proof leading to certain results. This praise is directed to Allah, who alone creates the genera of subjects and predicates without conditions. Then follows the salutation upon the Prophet Muhammad, described as the master of eloquent logic (mantiq fasih baligh), who brought the boundaries of Sharia and explained its definitions. The glossator then transitions to his purpose: these are ‘taqayid’ (notes) and ‘taqarir’ (reports) written upon the commentary of al-Sullam by al-Bannani. He praises al-Bannani's commentary for balancing brevity and solidity, refining expressions, and clarifying meanings. He notes that the commentary makes difficult concepts accessible, yet its deeper meanings (its ‘brides’) remain veiled, requiring a commentator to unveil them – which is the role of his gloss.

Key Terms
تقييد
شرح
سُلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To summarize the commentary for beginners
B) To criticize the commentary and propose new ideas
C) To unveil the hidden (veiled) meanings of the commentary
D) To provide a literal translation of al-Sullam

Key Takeaway
A glossator's introduction establishes the purpose of unveiling deeper meanings in a commentary that, while excellent, still requires further clarification.

Structure and Etiquette of a Traditional Islamic Preface
Author explains his reason for writing the hashiya and his humility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the structural components and scholarly etiquette in a traditional Islamic preface (muqaddima).

Core Idea
A scholarly preface reveals the author's humility, motivation, and reliance on divine guidance.

This passage introduces al-Bannani's gloss on al-Sullam. It is not just a rhetorical flourish; it establishes the author's scholarly credentials through humility and proper procedure. Understanding its parts helps us appreciate how Islamic scholars approached writing and sought divine support.

Guided Path
1
Open the preface
Identify the opening invocations: basmala, hamdalah, shahada, salawat. What purpose do they serve?
They consecrate the work and align it with Islamic tradition.
2
Identify the author's motive
Find the reason al-Bannani decided to write this gloss. Who requested it? Why did he initially refuse?
His reluctance shows scholarly caution and humility.
3
Examine the role of istikharah
Notice that the author sought Allah's guidance before proceeding. Why is this significant in scholarly practice?
It demonstrates reliance on divine will and seeking blessing.
4
Analyze the author's humility and acknowledgement of critics
How does al-Bannani preempt criticism? What does he say about those who might attack his work?
He admits his limited capacity and appeals to the intelligent reader's generosity.
5
Conclude with the closing prayer
What does the author ask for at the end?
He prays for a good outcome and divine assistance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله العظيم ونشكره جل جلاله على ما ألهم، ونشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، ونشهد أن سيدنا محمداً خير نبي بعثه وأرسله صلى الله وسلم عليه وعلى آله الأطهار، وصحابته المهاجرين والأنصار؛ وبعد:

فهذه تقاييد تتشوّف لعرائس خدورها الأذهان، وتقارير تتشرف بسماع مبانيها الآذان، موضوعةٌ على شرح السلم» للإمام الرباني، الحائز قصب السبق في استخراج فرائد الفوائد من بحر المعاني، أبي عبد الله سيدي محمد بن الحسن البناني - أسكنه الله تعالى بفضله ومنه دارَ التهاني، فيا له من شرح جمع بين الإيجاز وإحكام المباني، وتحرير التقول وتنقيح المعاني، يقرب للأفهام ما كان شموساً شموعاً، ويقيد المطلق ويطلق ما كان تقييده ممنوعاً، بيد أنَّ عرائسه محجبةٌ في الخدور، تفتقر في الاطلاع عليها لمن يكشف عنها الستور.
فَهَذَا تَقْيِيدٌ عَلَى النَّظْمِ المَوْسُومِ بِـ : السُّلَّم المُرَوْنَق»، أَلَجَّ عَلَيَّ فِيهِ مَنْ لَا بُدَّ مِنْ إِسْعَافِه، وَبِاللهِ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى أَعْتَصِم، مِنْ كُلِّ مَا يُشِينُ وَيَصِم.
فطلب مني حُذَاق الأصحاب، ممَّن له ولوع بتحقيق دقائق هذا الكتاب، أن أضع عليه حاشية تسفر عن وجوه خرائده اللثام، وتجعل غوامض مسائله على طرف الثمام، فأجبته بأني لست من أهل هذا المرام، ولا طاقة لي بالخوض في هذه البحور العِظام، ومَن حاول ما ليس في طوقه، عجب النَّاس من حمقه، فألح في الطلب، وأشار إلى الاستخارة في السبب، فاستخرت الله تعالى في المرغوب، وأجبته إذ ذاك للمطلوب.
هذا؛ وقد علمتُ أنّي لا أسلم من منتقد يتعلق بطوقي، يعتقد في نفسه أنَّه في المعرفة فوقي، فأقر له بقصر الباع، وقِلَّة النظر والاطلاع، لكنَّ الذَّكي الماهر، يحمل الكلام القاصر على وجه ظاهر، فإنَّ سيد الأكياس، مَن صوَّب خطأ النَّاس، ومَنِ اتَّسع علمه قلَّ إنكاره، فرُبَّ مُنكَرٍ لا تُقالُ عثاره، والكريمُ حليته الغَضُّ ، واللَّئيمُ مزيَّته العضُ، جعلنا الله تعالى مِنَ الَّذين يستمعون القول فيتّبعون أحسنه، وختم علينا بالحسنى فضلاً منه ومنة، فهو المسؤول في المبدأ والتَّمام والمطلوب منه الإعانة في المقصد والمرام.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, the Almighty, and we thank Him, exalted is His majesty, for what He inspired. We bear witness that there is no deity but Allah alone, with no partner. We bear witness that our master Muhammad is the best prophet He sent and commissioned; may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and upon his pure family and his Companions, the Emigrants and the Helpers. To proceed:

These are notes that yearn for minds to unveil their brides, and reports honored by ears hearing their structures, placed upon the commentary of 'al-Sullam' by the lordly Imam, who attained the prize in extracting unique benefits from the ocean of meanings, Abu Abdullah Sayyidi Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Bannani—may Allah the Exalted, by His bounty and grace, make him dwell in the abode of felicity. What a commentary it is, combining conciseness and solidity of structure, refinement of expression and precisification of meanings; it brings near to understanding what were elusive suns, and binds the absolute and releases what was prohibited to bind. Yet its brides are veiled in chambers, needing someone to uncover their curtains.

So this is a gloss upon the versified work known as 'al-Sullam al-Murawnaq', which was urged upon me by one whose request I must fulfill. And with Allah, glorified and exalted, I seek refuge from everything that disgraces and stains.

Then the skilled among my colleagues, those devoted to verifying the subtleties of this book, asked me to write a gloss that would remove the veil from the faces of its brides and bring its obscure problems to the fingertips. I replied that I am not among those qualified for this task, nor have I the capacity to plunge into these vast oceans; and whoever attempts what is beyond his capacity, people will marvel at his foolishness. But he persisted in the request and suggested seeking guidance (istikharah) in the matter. So I sought guidance from Allah the Exalted in the desired matter, and then I answered his request.

This, while I know that I will not escape a critic who will seize upon me, thinking himself above me in knowledge. I acknowledge to him my limited capacity and lack of insight and learning. But the intelligent and skilled will take deficient speech in a plausible manner, for the master of the wise is one who excuses people's errors. Whose knowledge is vast, his criticism is rare; many a criticized one cannot be saved from stumbling. The generous person his quality is forbearance, the vile person his trait is biting. May Allah the Exalted make us among those who listen to speech and follow the best of it, and seal for us goodness, as a favor and blessing from Him. He is the One asked from beginning to end, and from Him we seek aid in the aim and goal.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is the preface (muqaddima) of the gloss (hashiya) written by al-Bannani upon al-Akhdari's commentary on his own versified text 'al-Sullam al-Murawnaq'. The author begins with the basmala and praise of Allah, followed by the shahada and salawat upon the Prophet and his companions. He then describes his work: 'These are notes that yearn for minds to unveil their brides...' – a metaphorical description of the gloss as something that will reveal the hidden meanings of the original commentary. He praises the original commentary for its conciseness and precision but notes that its meanings are veiled, requiring explanation. He states that he wrote this gloss because someone ('one whose request I must fulfill') urged him, and he sought Allah's guidance. He then recounts that a group of skilled colleagues asked him to write a commentary (hashiya) to clarify difficult points. Initially he declined, citing his inadequacy, but after persistent requests and istikharah, he complied. He acknowledges that critics may attack him, but he humbly admits his shortcomings, hoping that the intelligent will interpret his words kindly. He concludes with a prayer for Allah to make him among those who listen and follow the best, and to grant him a good end. This preface establishes the author's humility, his motivation (peer request), and his awareness of potential criticism, setting the tone for the scholarly work that follows.

Key Terms
تقاييد (taqayid): Notes or glosses; the author's own term for his supercommentary (hashiya). [Note: No significant shift; common term for glosses.]
حاشية (hashiyah): A supercommentary or gloss on a commentary, written to clarify or expand upon it. [Note: No significant shift; standard term in the Islamic scholarly tradition.]
استخارة (istikharah): The act of seeking guidance from Allah through prayer when making a decision. [Note: No significant shift; religious practice.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the primary reason al-Bannani initially declined to write the gloss?
A) He did not have time.
B) He did not consider himself qualified.
C) He disliked the original commentary.
D) He wanted a co-author.

Key Takeaway
The preface is not merely formal; it establishes the author's humility, motivation, and reliance on Allah, setting the ethical tone for the scholarly work.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find another Islamic scholarly work (e.g., a tafsir, hadith commentary, or fiqh manual) and identify the standard components of its preface: basmala, hamdalah, salawat, motive, humility, istikharah if mentioned.
?
Write a brief one-paragraph preface for a hypothetical treatise on the virtues of prayer, following the structure and tone learned from al-Bannani's preface.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Purpose of a Hashiya: Clarifying Obscurity
Author explains why he wrote this commentary under pressure from colleagues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the stated purpose of a hashiya as seen in the author's preface and distinguish it from other forms of commentary.

Core Idea
A hashya unpacks the obscure; its author writes under obligation, not vanity.

Hashiya (super-commentary) is a key genre in Islamic scholarship, where a later scholar clarifies difficult passages in a primary text. This preface from al-Bajuri's hashya on al-Sullam al-Murawnaq reveals both the author's task and his attitude toward it. By studying this preface, you will learn to recognize the characteristic goals and circumstances that shape a hashiya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
The author refers to 'al-Sullam al-Murawnaq' - the original poem being annotated. This is a well-known text in Islamic logic.
The title al-Sullam al-Murawnaq is a poetic summary of logic.
2
Extract the stated goal
The author says he was asked to write a hashya 'that would unveil the faces of its obscure points and bring its difficult issues to the tip of the thumb.' This defines the hashya's purpose: clarifying obscurities and simplifying difficulties.
Unveiling the faces of obscure points means explaining what is unclear.
3
Note the social context
The request came from 'skilled companions' and the author initially refused, citing incapacity, but agreed after istikhara. This shows that a hashya was often commissioned by peers, not self-initiated.
Istikhara is a prayer for guidance when making a decision.
4
Distinguish hashya from other commentary genres
A sharrh is a full explanation; a hashya is a marginal note super-commentary. The author calls his work a taqyid (annotation) interchangeably with hashya. Compare the depth: a hashya assumes the reader knows the base text and main commentary.
Other genres include tafsir (Qur'anic commentary) and sharh (line-by-line explanation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَهَذَا تَقْيِيدٌ عَلَى النَّظْمِ المَوْسُومِ بِـ : السُّلَّم المُرَوْنَق»، أَلَجَّ عَلَيَّ فِيهِ مَنْ لَا بُدَّ مِنْ إِسْعَافِه ، وَبِاللهِ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى أَعْتَصِم ، مِنْ كُلِّ مَا يُشِينُ وَيَصِم . فطلب مني حُذَاق الأصحاب، ممَّن له ولوع بتحقيق دقائق هذا الكتاب، أن أضع عليه حاشية تسفر عن وجوه خرائده اللثام، وتجعل غوامض مسائله على طرف الثمام، فأجبته بأني لست من أهل هذا المرام، ولا طاقة لي بالخوض في هذه البحور العِظام، ومَن حاول ما ليس في طوقه، عجب النَّاس من حمقه، فألح في الطلب، وأشار إلى الاستخارة في السبب، فاستخرت الله تعالى في المرغوب، وأجبته إذ ذاك للمطلوب. هذا؛ وقد علمتُ أنّي لا أسلم من منتقد يتعلق بطوقي، يعتقد في نفسه أنَّه في المعرفة فوقي، فأقر له بقصر الباع، وقِلَّة النظر والاطلاع، لكنَّ الذَّكي الماهر، يحمل الكلام القاصر على وجه ظاهر، فإنَّ سيّد الأكياس، مَن صوَّب خطأ النَّاس، ومَنِ اتَّسع علمه قلَّ إنكاره، فرُبَّ مُنكَرٍ لا تُقالُ عثاره، والكريمُ حِليته الغَضُّ ، واللَّئيمُ مزيَّته العضُ، جعلنا الله تعالى مِنَ الَّذين يستمعون القول فيتّبعون أحسنه، وختم علينا بالحسنى فضلاً منه ،ومنة، فهو المسؤول في المبدأ والتَّمام والمطلوب منه الإعانة في المقصد والمرام.
This is an annotation on the poem known as al-Sullam al-Murawnaq. Someone whom I must oblige pressed me regarding it, and I seek refuge in Allah from everything that disgraces and stains. So the skilled among my companions, who is fond of verifying the subtleties of this book, asked me to write a hashya on it that would unveil the faces of its obscure points and bring its difficult issues to the tip of the thumb. I answered him that I am not of the people of this aspiration, nor do I have the capacity to wade into these great oceans – whoever attempts what is beyond his capacity, people marvel at his foolishness. But he persisted in the request and suggested istikhara regarding the matter, so I performed istikhara to Allah in the desired thing, and I answered him then for what was sought. And I knew that I will not be safe from a critic who will seize my neck, thinking himself above me in knowledge. So I acknowledge my shortcoming, lack of insight and knowledge. But the intelligent and skilled person carries weak speech on a manifest aspect. Indeed, the master of the clever is one who considers people's mistakes acceptable. Whose knowledge is vast, his denial is minimal. There is much that is rejected whose stumble is not forgiven. The generous person's ornament is gentleness, the base person's trait is harshness. May Allah make us of those who listen to speech and follow the best of it, and seal us with good, as a favor from Him and a grace. He is the one asked from beginning to end, and from Him is sought assistance in purpose and aim.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his hashya on al-Sullam al-Murawnaq. He begins by stating that this is an annotation (taqyid) on the poem, and that he was pressured by someone he could not refuse. He then relates that a skilled colleague asked him to write a commentary that would clarify the poem's obscurities. The author initially refused, claiming he was not capable, but after the colleague insisted and suggested istikhara, he complied. He acknowledges that he will face critics, but hopes that the intelligent will interpret his shortcomings favorably. He praises those who are forgiving and condemns harshness. He concludes by asking Allah to make him among those who follow the best of speech and to grant him success.

حَاشِيَة

C) To translate the poem into another language.
D) To recite the poem publicly.

Key Takeaway
A hashiya is written to elucidate difficult passages, often at the behest of others, and the author typically expresses humility about his ability.

Scholarly Humility and the Etiquette of Accepting a Task
Author explains why he wrote this commentary under pressure from colleagues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly values of humility, istikhara, and tolerance of criticism as expressed in Islamic academic prefaces.

Core Idea
True scholars decline praise, seek Allah's guidance, and expect fair critique.

This preface not only introduces the work but also models the adab (etiquette) of a scholar. The author's initial refusal, recourse to istikhara, acknowledgment of limitations, and plea for charitable interpretation all reflect core Islamic scholarly virtues. Understanding these values enriches our appreciation of the intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author's initial refusal
The author says 'I am not of the people of this aspiration, nor do I have the capacity to wade into these great oceans.' This shows humility and self-awareness.
This is a common trope in Islamic prefaces, but here it is sincere as he eventually agrees.
2
Note the role of istikhara
The colleague suggested istikhara (prayer for guidance), and after performing it, the author agreed. This highlights reliance on divine guidance in scholarly decisions.
Istikhara is a Sunnah practice when choosing between options.
3
Extract the expectation of criticism
The author anticipates a critic who will 'seize my neck' but hopes that 'the intelligent and skilled person carries weak speech on a manifest aspect.' He asks for leniency.
This reflects the Islamic principle that scholars should be forgiving of others' shortcomings.
4
Identify the praised trait
The author says 'the generous person's ornament is gentleness, the base person's trait is harshness.' He encourages gentleness in criticism.
This aligns with prophetic Hadith on leniency and mercy.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
15 min
The Basmala: Declarative or Performative? Objection and Resolution
Dialectical argument on basmala's sentence type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria for distinguishing declarative from performative sentences and evaluate the basmala sentence's classification using the objections and responses presented.

Core Idea
The basmala performs an act of seeking help; its primary meaning is not the action itself.

In this lesson, we explore a classic logical-linguistic problem: Is the basmala (Bismillah) a declarative sentence reporting a fact, or a performative utterance that brings about its content? Shaykh Isa al-Safawi raises a sharp objection: if it's declarative, its meaning should be true without uttering it; if performative, the action should occur upon utterance. The response from Abu Hafs al-Fasi and the subsequent criticism and refutation reveal nuanced distinctions that are vital for understanding the role of basmala in Islamic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sentence categories
Extract from the objection the definitions: a declarative (khabar) sentence reports a state of affairs true independently of utterance; a performative (insha') sentence creates its content upon utterance.
This classification is foundational in Arabic rhetoric and logic.
2
Apply the criteria to the basmala
Test the basmala against each category. For declarative: part of its meaning (accompaniment and seeking help) depends on utterance, so it fails. For performative: the action (e.g., slaughter) does not occur by merely saying the basmala, so it also fails.
The objection targets the specific estimation of the attached term (e.g., 'I slaughter') rather than general.
3
Analyze Abu Hafs's response
He chooses performative, but for the secondary meaning (seeking help or accompaniment) signified by the preposition 'ba'. The original sentence meaning becomes secondary, similar to how qualifications become primary in declarative sentences per Abd al-Qahir al-Jurjani.
This shifts the focus from the action verb to the instrumental meaning of the preposition.
4
Examine al-Hilali's criticism
He argues: (1) accompaniment is a relation between the composition and the name, so if the action is delayed, accompaniment is delayed; (2) the 'ba' of seeking help implies the action occurs with the instrument, so seeking help cannot precede the action.
This criticism attempts to show the response is inconsistent with the usual meaning of accompaniment and instrumentality.
5
Evaluate the refutation
The author responds: the two associated things in accompaniment are the person and the name (not the action), which precede the action; and seeking help in the linguistic sense ('seeking aid') is a mental attempt to gain power, which naturally precedes the action. Thus the response is sound.
This resolves the temporal objections by redefining the relata and the nature of seeking help.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (بِسْمِ اللَّهِ) الكلامُ في البسملة بحر زاخر، غاص في لجج بحره الأوائل والأواخر، واستخرجوا منه جواهر تزري بالنُّجوم الزَّوَاهر ، فلنقتصر على إشكال أورده الفاضل الشيخ عيسى الصَّفوي شيخ العبادي رحمهما الله على تقدير المتعلق خاصا مناسباً لما جعلتِ التّسمية مبدأ له، كما ذهب إليه الزَّمخشري ومَن وافقه . حاصله : أنَّ جملة البسملة لا بدَّ أن تكون خبريَّةٌ أو إنشائيَّةٌ ؛ ضرورة انحصار الكلام في الخبر والإنشاء: فإن كانت خبريَّةً توجّه عليه : أنَّ من لازم الخبر الصَّادق أن يتحقق مدلوله في نفس الأمر بدونه، ويكون هو حكاية عنه، كما صرح بذلك العلامة التفتازاني وغيره، وجملة البسملة ليست بهذه الصفة؛ لأنَّ مِن تتمَّة مدلولها مصاحبة الاسم والاستعانة به، ولا يقع ذلك إلَّا بالتلفظ به. وإن كانت إنشائيَّةً توجّه عليه أنَّ مِن لازم الإنشاء أن يقارن وجوده حصول مدلوله، وهذه الجملة ليست كذلك ؛ لأنَّ مدلولها وهو حصول التأليف مصحوباً بالاسم الشَّريف لا يقع بمجرَّد النُّطق بها ؛ لأنَّ نحو: «الأكل، والسفر والذَّبح ممَّا ليس بقول لا يحصل بالبسملة، فكيف يقدر مثلاً: «أَذْبَحُ» أو : «أُسَافِرُ بِاسْمِ اللهِ» بقصد الإنشاء. وإنَّما أورد الإشكال على تقدير المتعلق خاصا ؛ لأنَّه لا إشكال في الإنشائية على تقديره عاما ؛ لحصول الابتداء بالبسملة بمجرد النُّطق بها . وأجاب عن هذا الإشكال شيخ بعض شيوخنا أبو حفص الفاسي عملته بما نصه : أقول : يجاب باختيار أنَّها إنشائيَّةٌ ، وأنَّها لإنشاء متعلّقها الذي هو الاستعانة أو المصاحبة؛ يعني : اللَّذين هما مدلول «الباء»، ولا يلزم أن يكون الأصل الذي هو الجملة غير مقصود أصلاً، بل يكون مقصوداً تبعاً، وإذا كانتِ الجملُ الخبريَّةُ مع بقائها على حالها يكون المقصود الأصلي منها المتعلّق الذي قيد به مضمونها ـ حتى قال الشيخ عبد القاهر في دلائل الإعجاز»: «إنَّ النَّفي إذا دخل على كلام قيد بقيد ما ، يتوجه إلى ذلك القيد، ... وكذا الإثبات، فما من كلام فيه أمرٌ زائد على مجرد إثبات شيء لشيء أو نفيه عنه إلَّا وهو الغرضُ الأصلي والمقصود مِنَ الكلام». فكيف لا يكون الأمر كذلك مع التصرُّف فيها بالنقل عن معناها الأصلي، فالمقصود بجملة «بسم الله» الاستعانة بالاسم الشَّريف على ما يُراد مِنَ الفعل، أو المصاحبة له عند إرادة الشروع فيه، والمقصود الأصلي قبل النقل صار بعده تبعاً . وزعم بعض أفاضل العصر ونبهائه - يعني : الهلالي - أنَّ هذا الوجه المختار لا يصح : - أمَّا أَوَّلاً : فلأنَّ المصاحبة نسبة بين متصاحبين، فتأخُرهُما ، أو تأخر أحدهما ملزوم لتأخرها، والمتصاحبات هنا : التأليف والاسم الشَّريف، فإذا تأخر التأليف ونحوه عن النُّطق بالبسملة تأخَّرت مصاحبة الاسم؛ ضرورةً توقف النسبة على وجود المنتسبين . - وأما ثانياً : فإنَّ «باء» الاستعانة ـ كما قرر في محله الداخلة على آلة الفعل الحقيقيَّة ؛ هي نحو: «كَتَبْتُ بِالقَلَمِ»، أو المجازية نحو : فَعَلْتُ هَذَا بِعَوْنِ اللهِ تعالى، والاستعانة بالآلة إنَّما تكون حالة الفعل لا قبله، وتأخر الفعل مستلزم تأخرها ؛ كما في قولك: «سَأَكْتُبُ بِالقَلَمِ»، فجعل الجملة لإنشاء الاستعانة المفهومة مِنَ الباء) غلط نشأ من توهم أنَّها بمعنى: «طلب العون»؛ كما في: «أَسْتَعِينُ بِاللهِ»، وليس ذلك معناها، وإنما معناها إيقاع الفعل بواسطة مدخولها . اهـ. وهذا الزعم غير صواب؛ لأنَّ : مبنى الإيراد في المصاحبة : توهم أخذها من حيث هي نسبة بين متصاحبين، وهما : التأليف والاسم الشَّريف، وليس كذلك، بل المتصاحبان: الشَّخصُ والاسمُ الشَّريف، ولا خفاء في تقدُّمهما على التأليف على جهة الاستعداد له؛ حيث كان المراد المصاحبة عند إرادة الفعل والعزم عليه . ومبنى الإيراد في الاستعانة توهم المغايرة بين الاستعانة بالمعنى اللُّغوي - و تو: «طلب العون - وبين مدلول «الباء»، وذلك ممَّا لا دليل عليه . فالصَّوابُ أنَّهما متحدان وطلب العون محاولة الاقتدار على الفعل، فهي سابقة عليه
His saying: 'In the name of Allah'. Discussion on the basmala is a vast ocean; the predecessors and successors dived into the depths of its sea and extracted from it jewels that outshine the brilliant stars. So let us confine ourselves to an objection raised by the virtuous Shaykh Isa al-Safawi, the teacher of al-Abbadi, may Allah have mercy on them, based on the estimation of the attached term being specific, appropriate for what the naming was made a beginning for, as al-Zamakhshari and those who agreed with him held. Its summary: The basmala sentence must be either declarative or performative, due to the necessity that speech is confined to declarative and performative. If it is declarative, it is subject to the criticism that it is a necessary property of a true declarative that its signification is actualized in reality without it, and it is a report about it, as al-Taftazani and others explicitly stated. And the basmala sentence does not have this quality, because part of its complete signification is the accompaniment of the name and seeking help by it, and that does not occur except by uttering it. And if it is performative, it is subject to the criticism that it is a necessary property of a performative that its existence is concomitant with the actualization of its signification, and this sentence is not like that, because its signification, which is the actualization of the composition accompanied by the noble name, does not occur merely by pronouncing it, because things like eating, traveling, and slaughtering, which are not speech, are not actualized by the basmala. So how can one estimate, for example, 'I slaughter' or 'I travel in the name of Allah' with the intention of performative? He only raised the objection on the estimation of the attached term being specific, because there is no objection regarding the performative on the estimation of it being general, due to the beginning with the basmala occurring merely by pronouncing it. And a shaykh of some of our teachers, Abu Hafs al-Fasi, may Allah have mercy on him, answered this objection with the following text: I say: It can be answered by choosing that it is performative, and that it is for the creation of its attached term which is seeking help or accompaniment, meaning the two which are the signification of the 'ba', and it is not necessary that the original which is the sentence is not intended at all; rather, it is intended secondarily. And if declarative sentences, while remaining as they are, have their primary intent as the attached term that qualifies their content – as Shaykh Abd al-Qahir said in Dala'il al-I'jaz: 'Indeed, negation, when it enters a speech qualified by a qualification, is directed to that qualification, ... and likewise affirmation. There is no speech containing something additional to mere affirmation or negation of something to something except that it is the primary purpose and intent of the speech.' So how could it not be the case with transformation of them by transferring from their original meaning? Thus the intent of the sentence 'Bismillah' is seeking help by the noble name for the intended action, or accompaniment of it when intending to start it, and the original intent before the transfer became secondary after it. And one of the virtuous of the age and its eminent ones – meaning al-Hilali – claimed that this chosen view is not sound: First, because accompaniment is a relation between two associated things, so their delay or the delay of one of them necessitates its delay. And the two associated things here are the composition and the noble name. So if the composition and the like are delayed after the utterance of the basmala, the accompaniment of the name is delayed, necessarily because the relation depends on the existence of the relata. Second, because the 'ba' of seeking help – as established in its place – enters upon the real instrument of the action, like 'I wrote with the pen', or metaphorical like 'I did this with the help of Allah Almighty'. And seeking help by the instrument only occurs at the time of the action, not before it, and the delay of the action necessitates its delay, as in your saying 'I will write with the pen'. So making the sentence for the creation of seeking help understood from the 'ba' is a mistake arising from the misconception that it means 'seeking aid', as in 'I seek help from Allah', but that is not its meaning; rather, its meaning is the occurrence of the action by means of its object. End. And this claim is not correct, because: The basis of the objection regarding accompaniment is the misconception of taking it as a relation between two associated things, which are the composition and the noble name, but it is not so. Rather, the two associated things are the person and the noble name, and there is no doubt about their precedence over the composition in terms of preparedness for it, since what is intended is accompaniment at the time of intending the action and resolving upon it. And the basis of the objection regarding seeking help is the misconception of a difference between seeking help in the linguistic sense – which is 'seeking aid' – and the signification of the 'ba', and there is no evidence for that. The correct view is that they are identical, and seeking aid is an attempt to gain power over the action, so it is prior to it.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical discussion from the commentary on the opening of the matn, addressing the nature of the basmala sentence. The author first presents an objection raised by Shaykh Isa al-Safawi. The objection is based on the premise that every sentence must be either declarative (khabariyya) or performative (insha'iyya). If the basmala is declarative, then its content should be true independently of utterance, but the basmala's meaning includes accompaniment and seeking help, which only occur upon utterance. If it is performative, then its signification should be actualized immediately upon utterance, but for actions like eating or slaughtering, the act does not occur by merely saying 'Bismillah'. The objection is specifically for when the attached term (al-muta'allaq) is considered specific (like 'I slaughter'), not general. Then the author quotes the answer of Abu Hafs al-Fasi: the basmala is performative, but its performative force is for creating the attached meaning (seeking help or accompaniment) which is signified by the preposition 'ba'. The original sentence meaning (the action) becomes secondary, similar to how in declarative sentences the qualification (qayd) often becomes the primary intent, as cited from Abd al-Qahir al-Jurjani. Then al-Hilali criticizes this answer on two points: first, regarding accompaniment, he argues that it is a relation between two things (composition and the name), so if the action is delayed, the accompaniment is also delayed; second, regarding seeking help, he argues that the 'ba' of instrumentality indicates that help occurs during the action, not before. The author then refutes al-Hilali: for accompaniment, the two associated things are the person and the name, which exist before the action; for seeking help, the linguistic meaning is 'seeking aid', which is a mental attempt to gain power, and thus precedes the action. Thus the original response stands.

Key Terms
البسملة
الخبر
الإنشاء
الاستعانة
المصاحبة
الباء

D) It would require a verb.

Key Takeaway
The basmala sentence is performative for its secondary meaning of seeking help or accompaniment, resolving the apparent contradiction with temporal criteria.

Three Reasons for Beginning with al-Hamd
Author explains three reasons for starting the poem with praise of Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the three reasons given by the commentator for beginning with al-Hamd instead of a verbal sentence.

Core Idea
The choice of al-Hamd is rooted in Quranic imitation, phonetic comprehensiveness, and contextual eloquence.

In this passage, the commentator elucidates why the poet began with "al-Ḥamd" rather than directly naming Allah. He provides three distinct reasons, each touching on different aspects: Quranic precedent, the physical articulation of the word, and the principle of rhetorical appropriateness. Understanding these reasons deepens our appreciation of the structure of Islamic scholarly texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three reasons
Read the passage and locate the three reasons given for beginning with al-Hamd. They are introduced by "li-anna" or bullet points in the translation.
The reasons are: Quranic preface, phonetic comprehensiveness, and context necessitating praise.
2
Examine the first reason: Quranic imitation
The commentator points out that the Quran itself starts with praise (al-Fatiha). Beginning with al-Hamd imitates the divine book.
This ties the work to the highest standard of eloquence.
3
Examine the second reason: phonetic comprehensiveness
The word al-Hamd contains three letters from different articulation points: ḥā’ (throat), mīm (lips), and dāl (tongue). Thus, every part of the speech apparatus participates.
This is a subtle linguistic argument about the word's completeness.
4
Examine the third reason: situational context and ta'assī
The context of beginning a work of knowledge calls for praise, and one should follow the prophetic example (ta’assī). The commentator stresses eloquence as matching speech to the situation.
This explains why the author did not begin with Allah's name despite its greater importance.
5
Synthesize: why not start with 'Allah'?
The commentator explicitly says that although the name Allah is more important, eloquence (balāgha) requires that speech be appropriate to the context. Starting with al-Hamd fits the occasion of commencing a work.
This shows the sophistication of the author's rhetorical choices.

His statement: 'He came with praise' – he only came with praise, while what is understood from the expression is that the praised thing here is the blessing of knowledge, and Allah said: 'If you are grateful, I will surely increase you' [Ibrahim: 7]; because: - The preface of the Noble Quran is adorned with the beauty of praise. - And because 'al-hamd' contains the throat letter ḥā’, the lip letter mīm, and the tongue letter dāl, so that no articulation point is completely without its share. - And because the context necessitates praise, along with the intention of following the example. He did not mention the word of majesty even though it is more important in itself, for eloquence is nothing but matching speech to the requirement of the situation.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage explains why the author of the poem began with the word 'al-Ḥamd' (praise) rather than directly saying 'Allāh' or using a verbal sentence. The commentator gives three reasons. First, the Quran itself is adorned with praise at its opening, so imitating the Quran is virtuous. Second, the word 'al-Ḥamd' contains three different articulation points: the throat (ḥā’), the lips (mīm), and the tongue (dāl), so every part of the speech apparatus is involved. Third, the context of beginning a work of knowledge calls for praise, and one should follow the prophetic example (ta’assī). The commentator also notes that the author did not mention the name of Allah at the very beginning, even though it is more important, because eloquence requires matching the speech to the situation.

Resolving Apparent Contradictions via Semantic Disambiguation
Commentator provides four answers to the objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real, customary, and relational meanings of a key term and apply these distinctions to resolve conflicting textual evidence in Islamic scholarship.

Core Idea
Apparent contradictions dissolve when key terms are recognized as having multiple valid meanings.

When Islamic texts seem to conflict, commentators often reconcile them by showing that a crucial term is being used in different senses. In this passage, the commentator resolves an objection to opening a work with both the basmalah and hamdalah by distinguishing four meanings of 'beginning.' Understanding this method equips you to handle similar conflicts in fiqh, hadith, and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Find the objection in the passage: 'beginning with one precludes beginning with the other.' Note the apparent logical conflict.
The objection assumes a single, literal meaning of 'beginning.'
2
Understand the Four Answers
List the four answers: (1) customary beginning, (2) general meaning covering real and relational, (3) real for basmalah and relational for hamdalah, (4) beginning with both as perfection.
Each answer reinterprets 'beginning' differently.
3
Analyze Each Interpretation
For each answer, clarify what 'beginning' means. Customary: from start of task to main objective. Real: first utterance. Relational: relative priority.
The third answer combines two meanings.
4
Assess Textual Support
Notice that the commentator mentions the Quran and strength of hadiths as grounds for preferring certain interpretations.
The basmalah is given real beginning because its hadith is stronger and it appears first in the Quran.

(۲) ۲ - أَوْ بِحَمْلِهِ فِيهِمَا عَلَى : الأَعَمِّ مِنَ الحَقِيقِيِّ وَالإِضَافِيِّ . ـ أَوْ بِحَمْلِهِ فِي البَسْمَلَةِ عَلَى : الحَقِيقِيِّ، وَفِي الحَمْدَلَةِ عَلَى : الإِضَافِيِّ القَرِيبِ مِنْهُ ; بِأَنْ يُذْكَرَ الحَمْدُ عَقِبَ البَسْمَلَةِ مُتَّصِلاً بِهَا ; كَمَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ القُرْآنُ، فَهُوَ مُبَيِّن لِكَيفِيَّةِ العَمَلِ بِالحَدِيثَيْنِ . ٤ - عَلَى أَنَّ الابْتِدَاءَ بِهِمَا مَعاً مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى الكَمَالِ. قوله : (يُفَوِّتُ الِابْتِدَاءَ بِالْآخَرِ) أي: لأنَّ الابتداء بالشَّيء جَعْلُه أوَّل ما يذكر، وذلك ينفي جعل غيره كذلك . قوله : (إِلَى حِيْنِ الأَخْذِ فِي المَقْصُودِ) أي: وهو يَسَعُ البسملة والحمدلة. قوله : (أَوْ بِحَمْلِهِ فِي البَسْمَلَةِ عَلَى الحَقِيقِي) وجه تخصيص البسملة بالحقيقي على هذا : أنَّ حديثها أقوى ولورودها في القرآن على هذا المنوال. قوله : (عَلَى أَنَّ الاِبْتِدَاءَ قال شيخنا أبو منصور : هذا جواب رابع.
And what they objected: that beginning with one of them precludes beginning with the other, is answered: 1- By interpreting 'beginning' in both as customary, which is considered extended from the time of starting the thing to the time of taking up the intended purpose. 2- Or by interpreting it in both as more general than the real and the relational. Or by interpreting it in the basmalah as real, and in the hamdalah as relational close to it; such that the hamd is mentioned after the basmalah connected to it, as the Quran indicates, so it clarifies how to act upon the two hadiths. 4- That beginning with both together is interpreted as perfection. His saying: (precludes beginning with the other) means: because beginning with a thing is making it the first thing mentioned, and that negates making another likewise. His saying: (to the time of taking up the intended purpose) means: and it accommodates the basmalah and hamdalah. His saying: (or by interpreting it in the basmalah as real) the reason for specifying the basmalah with the real in this is that its hadith is stronger and because it occurs in the Quran in this manner. His saying: (that beginning) our teacher Abu Mansur said: this is a fourth answer.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) addressing an objection to the opening of a matn. The objection states that beginning with both the basmalah and the hamdalah is impossible because starting with one precludes starting with the other. The commentator gives four answers. The first answer interprets 'beginning' in both as 'customary beginning,' which extends from the start of the action to the point of taking up the intended purpose, thus accommodating both. The second answer interprets 'beginning' as more general than both the real and relational meanings. The third answer, marked by a dash, interprets 'beginning' in the basmalah as real (i.e., actual first utterance) and in the hamdalah as relational (i.e., close to it in time), so the hamdalah follows immediately after the basmalah, as seen in the Quran. The fourth answer says that beginning with both together is a matter of perfection rather than actual temporal priority. The commentator then explains the glosses: the first gloss clarifies that 'precludes' means making one thing the first negates another being first. The second gloss says the customary beginning accommodates both. The third gloss explains why the basmalah is assigned the real beginning: its hadith is stronger and it appears in the Quran in that manner. The fourth gloss notes that a scholar called this a fourth answer. All examples and reasoning are rooted in Islamic textual traditions (Quran and hadith), not secular examples.

Commentators resolve apparent contradictions by showing that a key term can have different valid meanings, each applicable in a specific context.

Analyzing the Sea Metaphor in Islamic Logical Texts
Commentator explains the sea metaphor for meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze a metaphorical expression in an Islamic logic text and explain its pedagogical function, as exemplified by the 'bahr al-ma'ani' metaphor.

Core Idea
The sea metaphor in logic texts reminds us that rigorous tools are needed to navigate the vastness of meanings.

This passage from a commentary on a logic poem uses the striking image of a 'sea of meanings' to convey the depth of the subject. The commentator dissects this metaphor, showing how it is built and why it is effective. In this lesson, you will learn to recognize and analyze such metaphors, understanding how they serve not just as decoration but as essential pedagogical devices that underscore the necessity of logical tools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base metaphor
Find the two things being compared: meanings (ma'ani) and the sea (bahr). The commentator says the idafa (construct phrase) is one of similitude.
The comparison is explicit: meanings are like the sea in vastness.
2
Analyze the specific words chosen
Notice 'lujaj' (deep waters) and 'hawd' (watering place). The commentator explains these as amplification (tarshih) of the simile, intensifying the image.
These details make the metaphor more vivid and concrete.
3
Classify the types of isti'ara
The commentator identifies three rhetorical devices: isti'ara bi al-kinaya (allusive metaphor) where the intellect is likened to a ship, isti'ara takhiliyya (imaginative metaphor) in mentioning the sea and deep waters, and tajrid (abstraction) in 'ma'ani' itself.
This shows the layered complexity of metaphorical language in Islamic scholarship.
4
Explain the pedagogical purpose
The metaphor conveys that meanings (especially in logic) are vast and cannot be navigated without a tool. Here, the intellect (or logic) acts as the ship. This justifies the study of logic as a necessary instrument.
It is a call to equip oneself with proper methods to avoid drowning in confusion.
5
Apply to another example
Think of a similar metaphor in another Islamic science, e.g., 'the ocean of hadith' or 'the mine of fiqh'. How does that metaphor function? What tool does it imply?
This exercise trains you to see pedagogical metaphors as arguments for methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أتى بالصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عند ذكر اسمه الشريف؛ لحديث: «البخيل كل البخيل من ذكرت عنده فلم يصل علي»، وحديث: «رغم أنف رجل ذكرت عنده فلم يصل علي» أخرجه الترمذي وغيره. والإضافة في بحر المعاني من إضافة المشبه به إلى المشبه؛ أي: يخوض في المعاني التي هي كالبحر في انساع كل منهما انساعاً يحتاج في سلوكه إلى آلة، وذكر اللجج والحوض ترشيح للتشبيه. ويحتمل أن يكون شبه في نفسه الحجا الذي هو العقل بالسفينة في التوصل بكل منهما إلى المراد، وهذه استعارة بالكتابة، وذكر اللجج والبحر استعارة تخييلية، والمعاني تجريد، وهو أن تذكر ما يلائم المشبه. واللجج جمع: «لجة»، وهي: معظم الماء. ومعنى البيت: تأبيد الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بدوام تفكر العقل في مسائل العلم، وذلك بدوام العلماء، ودوامهم لقيام الساعة؛ لقول صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا تزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق لا يضرهم من خالفهم حتى يأتي أمر الله» أي: الساعة كما في بعض الطرق. قلت: يحتمل أنه قد قرن بينهما لفظاً، وأسقط السلام خطأ، أو ذهب على أنه لا كراهة في ذلك؛ قال الأجهوري: شاع في كتب المتقدمين من أهل مذهبنا وغيرهم قولهم: «قال عليه السلام ونحوه مقتصرين على السلام»، وأخبرني الثقة أنه رآه بخط الباجي كذلك، وإذا لم يكره إفراد السلام فالصلاة أولى. قوله: (وحديث: «رغم» ... إلخ) هذا الحديث أخرجه الترمذي عن أبي هريرة رضي الله تعالى عنه، ومعنى «رغم»: ألصق بالرغام؛ أي: التراب. قوله: (جمع: «لجة») أي: بضم اللام، وأما بفتحها فهو: الخصومة واختلاط الأصوات؛ قال الشاعر: [من الرجز] في لجة أمسك فلانا عن فل
He came with prayer upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, when mentioning his noble name, due to the hadith: 'The miser is utterly the one in whose presence I am mentioned and he does not pray upon me,' and the hadith: 'May his nose be rubbed in dust, a man in whose presence I am mentioned and he does not pray upon me.' Al-Tirmidhi and others reported it. The idafa in 'bahr al-ma'ani' is the idafa of the thing compared to the thing compared to it; i.e., he wades in meanings that are like the sea in their vastness, each needing a tool for navigation. Mention of 'lujaj' and 'hawd' is amplification of the simile. It is possible that he likened in himself the intellect to a ship in reaching the desired end through each, and this is an isti'ara bi al-kinaya, and mentioning 'lujaj' and 'bahr' is an isti'ara takhiliyya, and 'ma'ani' is tajrid, which is mentioning what is suitable to the simile. 'Lujaj' is plural of 'lujja', meaning the main body of water. The meaning of the line: Continuity of prayer upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, through the continuity of the mind's reflection in the matters of knowledge, and that is through the continuity of the scholars, and their continuity until the establishment of the Hour, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'A group of my community will continue to be manifest upon the truth, not harmed by those who oppose them, until the command of Allah comes,' i.e., the Hour, as in some versions. I said: It is possible that he combined them verbally and omitted 'peace' by mistake, or he thought there is no dislike in that; al-Ujhuri said: It is common in the books of the early scholars of our school and others to say 'peace be upon him' exclusively, and a trustworthy person told me he saw it in the handwriting of al-Baji likewise, and if it is not disliked to single out 'peace', then 'prayer' is more appropriate. His saying: (And the hadith: 'rghima' etc.) This hadith was reported by al-Tirmidhi from Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, and the meaning of 'rghima' is: stuck to the dust. His saying: (Plural of 'lujja') i.e., with damm on the lam, but with fatha it means dispute and confusion of voices; the poet said: [in rajaz] 'In a lujja, restrain so-and-so from so-and-so.'
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening line of the poem, which begins with the basmala and praise of Allah, and then mentions invoking salat upon the Prophet when his name is spoken. The commentator explains the reason for this practice by citing two hadiths that condemn those who neglect to send blessings upon the Prophet when his name is mentioned. The first hadith calls such a person extremely stingy, and the second threatens humiliation ('rghima'). These are followed by a rhetorical analysis of the phrase 'bahr al-ma'ani' (sea of meanings). The commentator explains the grammatical construction as one of simile, where 'meanings' are likened to a vast sea that one must navigate carefully. The mention of 'lujaj' (deep waters) and 'hawd' (watering place) reinforces the metaphor. He then offers an alternative interpretation: the poet likens the intellect to a ship that enables one to traverse this sea to reach understanding. This is classified as an isti'ara bi al-kinaya (allusive metaphor), while the mention of the sea and deep waters is an isti'ara takhiliyya (imaginative metaphor). The term 'ma'ani' itself is tajrid (abstraction), meaning one mentions something that suits the compared entity. The word 'lujaj' is defined as the plural of 'lujja', the deep part of water. The commentator then explains the overall meaning of the line: the continuity of salat upon the Prophet is tied to the continuity of scholars and their reflection on knowledge, which continues until the Day of Judgment as indicated by the hadith that a group of the community will always be manifest on truth. A marginal note (by al-Bajuri) discusses a textual variant: whether the poet omitted 'wa sallim' (and peace) by mistake or intentionally, and notes that early scholars sometimes used only 'peace'. Another note explains the hadith about 'rghima' and the linguistic nuances of 'lujja'.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي
البحر
اللجة

Checkpoint

A) To indicate geographical features

The Enduring Group: Scholars or Mujahideen?
Commentary discusses the meaning of ta'ifa and different scholarly views on who they are.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main scholarly interpretations of the ta'ifa in the hadith and explain why the commentator favors the interpretation that they are the people of knowledge.

Core Idea
The enduring group (ta'ifa) combines knowledge and jihad; the commentator favors scholars.

This lesson dives into a classic hadith commentary that unpacks the identity of the ta'ifa – the group that remains manifest upon the truth until the Day of Judgment. By examining the commentator's analysis, you'll learn how scholars weigh evidence from different hadith versions to arrive at a preferred interpretation. This is a practical example of how Islamic scholarship resolves apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Locate the key terms
Find the phrases 'al-ta'ifa' and 'zahirina 'ala al-haqq' in the Arabic text. Notice how the commentator glosses 'zahirina' as 'ghalibin' (dominant) to clarify meaning.
2
Identify the two opinions
The commentator mentions two interpretations: (1) the ta'ifa are the people of knowledge (ahl al-'ilm) and (2) they are the mujahideen. Note the evidence cited for each: the hadith about understanding religion for the first, and the hadith about fighting for the second.
3
Determine the preferred opinion
The commentator states that the first opinion (scholars) is 'the most correct' (asahhuha). Identify the reason: the beginning of the hadith in some versions links ta'ifa to religious understanding.
4
Recognize the reconciliation
The commentator adds that there is no contradiction between knowledge and jihad – one can be both a scholar and a mujahid. This shows how he harmonizes the two views.
5
Examine the additional variant
Notice the reference to al-Daraqutni's version specifying the ta'ifa is in the Maghrib. Consider how this geographical detail does not change the core identity of the group.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: «لا تزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق» أي: غالبين على الحق؛ أي: لتمكنهم منه واتباعهم له. وقد اختلف ما المراد بالطائفة؟ فقيل: أهل العلم؛ لابتداء الحديث في بعض الطرق بقوله: من يرد الله به خيرا يفقهه في الدين وهو أصحها، وعليه درج هذا الشارح. وقيل: المجاهدون؛ كما يدل له حديث مسلم: «لن يبرح هذا الدين قائما، يقاتل عليه عصابة من المسلمين، حتى تقوم الساعة». ويمكن أن يقال: لا منافاة بين العلم والجهاد. وفي الدارقطني: عن سعد بن أبي وقاص: «لا تزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق في المغرب حتى تقوم الساعة». قوله: (حق) أي: متأكد، غاية.
His saying: 'A group of my community will continue to be manifest upon the truth' i.e., dominant over the truth; meaning, due to their grasp of it and their following it. And there has been disagreement about what is meant by 'the group'? It was said: the people of knowledge; because the hadith begins in some versions with his saying: 'Whomever Allah desires good for, He gives him understanding of the religion' – and this is the most correct opinion, and this commentator followed it. And it was said: the mujahideen; as indicated by the hadith of Muslim: 'This religion will continue to stand, fought for by a band of Muslims until the Hour is established.' And it can be said: there is no contradiction between knowledge and jihad. And in al-Daraqutni: from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: 'A group of my community will continue to be manifest upon the truth in the Maghrib until the Hour is established.' His saying: (truly) i.e., emphatic, extreme.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the hadith cited earlier about the ta'ifa (group) that will remain manifest upon the truth. The commentator begins by explaining the phrase 'zahirina 'ala al-haqq' as meaning they are dominant over the truth, because they firmly grasp and follow it. He then raises the question: who exactly is this ta'ifa? He presents two main opinions from the scholarly tradition. The first and preferred opinion, which the commentator himself follows, is that they are the scholars (ahl al-'ilm). This is supported by the beginning of the hadith in some versions, which speaks about Allah giving understanding of the religion to whomever He desires good. The second opinion identifies the ta'ifa as the mujahideen (those who fight in the path of Allah), citing a different hadith from Muslim that speaks of a group fighting to uphold the religion until the Hour. The commentator then reconciles these views by noting that there is no contradiction between being a scholar and a mujahid; one can be both. He also mentions a third version from al-Daraqutni that specifies the ta'ifa will be in the Maghrib (West). Finally, the commentator explains the word 'haqq' in the phrase 'zahirina 'ala al-haqq' as meaning emphatic or extreme, indicating the certainty of the truth they are upon.

Interpreting the Righteous Group Hadith
Commentator explains the hadith and its interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main interpretations of 'ta'ifa' in this hadith and explain how the commentator reconciles them.

Core Idea
The righteous group is defined by both knowledge and jihad—no contradiction.

This passage opens the commentary on a hadith that promises a group of Muslims will remain victorious on truth until the Hour. The commentator first clarifies key terms, then tackles the central question: Who exactly is this group? He presents two major interpretations and shows they are complementary, not conflicting.

Guided Path
1

لِقَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا تَزَالُ طَائِفَةٌ مِنْ أُمَّتِي ظَاهِرِينَ عَلَى الحَقِّ لَا يَضُرُّهُمْ مَنْ خَالَفَهُمْ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ أَمْرُ اللهِ» أَي : السَّاعَةُ كَمَا فِي بَعْضِ الطُّرُقِ . قوله: «لَا تَزَالُ طَائِفَةٌ مِنْ أُمَّتِي ظَاهِرِينَ عَلَى الحَقِّ») أي : غالبين على الحقِّ؛ أي: لتمكنهم منه واتباعهم له . وقدِ اختلف ما المراد بالطَّائفة؟ فقيل : أهل العلم؛ لابتداء الحديث في بعض الطرق بقوله : مَنْ يُرِدِ اللَّهُ بِهِ خَيْراً يُفَقِّهْهُ في الدِّينِ وهو أصحها، وعليه درج هذا الشارح. وقيل: المجاهدون؛ كما يدلُّ له حديث «مسلم» : «لَنْ يَبْرَحَ هَذَا الدِّينُ قَائِماً، يُقَاتِلُ عَلَيْهِ عِصَابَةٌ مِنَ المُسْلِمِينَ، حَتَّى تَقُومَ السَّاعَةُ» . ويمكن أن يقال : لا منافاة بين العلم والجهاد. وفي «الدارقطني»: عن سعد بن أبي وقاص : لَا تَزَالُ طَائِفَةٌ مِنْ أُمَّتِي ظَاهِرِينَ عَلَى الحَقِّ فِي المَغْرِب حَتَّى تَقُومَ السَّاعَةُ . قوله : (حَقِّ) أي: متأكد، غاية.
For his saying, peace be upon him: 'A group of my community will not cease to be manifestly victorious upon the truth, not harmed by those who oppose them, until the command of God comes' meaning: the Hour, as in some versions. His saying: 'A group of my community will not cease to be manifestly victorious upon the truth' meaning: dominant over the truth, i.e., due to their mastery of it and their following it. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a hadith cited by the poet in the opening of his logic poem. The commentator first clarifies that 'the command of God' in the hadith refers to the Hour, as indicated in some narrations. He then explains the phrase 'manifestly victorious upon the truth' as meaning that this group is dominant over the truth because they have mastered it and follow it. Second, it refers to the mujahidin, supported by a hadith in Muslim about a band fighting for the religion. He then reconciles the two by noting that there is no contradiction between knowledge and jihad. Finally, he glosses the word 'haqq' in the phrase 'zahirina 'ala al-haqq' as meaning 'assured' or 'extreme' to emphasize its certainty.
